اشرف البدایہ شرح ار به يه - بعد تنم ار... نام ہے کیونکہ ملک آزاد کرنے والے کا حق ہے اور قیمت شریعت کا حق ہے۔ کیونکہ کا فر نے جب عبد اللہ ، خدا کا غلام ہونے سے انکار کیا تو اللہ نے اس کو اس طرح بدلہ دیا کہ اپنے بندے کا غلام بنایا۔ یا رقیت عام لوگوں کا حق ہے۔ کیونکہ مجاہد بین جس طرح رقیق کے علاوہ سامان کو تقسیم کرتے ہیں اسی طرح رقیق بھی تقسیم کریں گے اور تصرف کا حکم اس قدر ہوتا ہے جتنا کہ تصرف کرنے والے کے قابو میں ہے اور وہ یہی ہے کہ اپنا حق دور کرے، نہ کہ غیر کا حق یعنی مولی صرف ملک دور کر سکتا ہے نہ کہ رقیت اور ملک متجری ہے۔ لہذا اعتاق بھی متجری ہوگا اور بات دراصل یہ ہے کہ تصرف اسی جگہ تک رہتا ہے۔ جہاں اسکی نسبت کی گئی ہو اور اس جگہ سے علاوہ کی طرف تجاوز کرنا اسی ضرورت سے ہو سکتا ہے کہ اس کی تجربی نہ ہو سکے اور یہاں ملک جو مولی کا حق ہے اسکی تجزی ہو سکتی ہے۔ جیسے بیع اور بیہ میں ظاہر ہے یعنی مثلاً آدھا غلام بیچا یا ہبہ کیا، تو بالا تفاق جائز ہے۔ پس اعتناق کا تصرف بھی اپنی اصل پر رہے گا۔ یعنی اگر آدھا آزاد کیا تو جائز ہے۔ آدھا ہی آزاد ہوگا۔
اور ر ہا غلام پر باقی حصہ کیلئے کمائی واجب ہونا تو اس وجہ سے ہے کہ باقی ٹکڑے کی مالیت اس غلام کے پاس رکی ہوئی ہے۔ لہذا ا۔ سے وصول کی جائے اور جس غلام پر کمائی کر کے ادا کرنا واجب ہے وہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک منزلہ مکاتب کے ہے۔ کیونکہ جب تاق کی نسبت غلام کے کسی جز کی طرف کی گئی تو باعتبار مشتق کے لازم آیا کہ پورے غلام میں اس کو ملکت حاصل ہو۔ یعنی غلام اپنی پوری ذات : مالک ہو جائے۔ اسلئے کہ عقیق متجری نہیں ہوتا ہے اور مولیٰ کی ملک کا کسی ٹکڑے میں باقی رہنا باعتبار رقیت کے اس بات کا تقاضا کرتا ہے کہ وہ پوری ذات کا مالک نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ ، قیت بھی متجری نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ یہاں دو باتیں جمع ہو گئیں ۔ ایک یہ کہ غلام اپنی پوری ذات کا مالک نہ ہو۔ دوم یہ کہ غلام کی پیاری ذات میں مولی کی ملک باقی رہے اور چونکہ دونوں دلیلوں پر عمل کرناممکن ہے۔ اسلئے ہم نے دونوں دلیلوں پر عمل کیا اور اس خدام کو ۔ کیا اب شہرایا۔ اسلئے کہ مکاتب ید اما الک ہوتا ہے اور رقبہ مملوک ہوتا ہے۔ پس ایسے ہی یہ بھی اپنی کمائی کا مالک ہے اور اپنی ذات کے مالک نہیں ہے اور جب مستعلی مکاتب کے مانند ہے تو اس کی کمائی بدل کتابت کے مانند ہوگی۔ لہذا مولیٰ کو یہ اختیاررہا کہ اس سے کمائی کرا کر باقی قیمت وصول کرے اور یہ بھی اختیار ہے کہ چاہے اس کو آزاد کر دے کیونکہ مکا تب بھی اس قابل ہوتا ہے کہ مولیٰ اس کو آزد کر دے۔ لیکن یہاں ایک سوال ہے وہ یہ کہ مستسعی اگر مکاتب کے مرتبہ میں ہے تو جس طرح مکاتب بدل کتابت سے عاجز ہونے کی صورت میں رقیق ہو جاتا ہے۔ اسی طرح مستسعی اگر کمائی سے عاجز ہو جائے تو اس کو بھی رقیق ہو جانا چاہئے ۔ حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے۔ جبکہ یہ غلام جس کا ایک جز آزاد ہو کر اس پر کمائی واجب ہوئی۔ اگر کمائی سے عاجز ہو جائے تو یہ رقیق نہیں کہا جاسکتا ۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں میں اتنا فرق ہے کہ اگر مکاتب اداء مال سے عاجز ہو تو وہ رقیق کر دیا جاتا ہے اور یہ غلام اگر کمائی سے عاجز ہو جائے تو رقیق نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔ وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ غلام آزاد کرنا اسقاط لا الی احد ہے۔ یعنی اس سے ملکیت ساقط کر نالا الی احد ہے اور اسقاط لا الی احد میں معاوضہ کے معنی نہیں پائے جاتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ معاوضہ دو آدمیوں کے درمیان متحقق ہوتا ہے اور یہاں صرف ایک آدمی ہے یعنی آزاد کرنے والا ۔ پس جب اس صورت میں معاوضہ کے معنی نہیں پائے گئے تو یہ نسخ کے قابل بھی نہیں ہے۔

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد باد
وليس في الطلاق ... الخ سے صاحبین اور امام شافعی کے قیاس فصار کا لطلاق والعفو عن القصاص والاستمیلاد کا جواب ہے۔ چنانچہ فرمایا کہ اعتناق کو طلاق اور عفو عن القصاص پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ طلاق اور نکاح کے درمیان یا قصاص اور محفو کے درمیان کوئی درمیانی حالت نہیں ہے۔ جیسا آزادی اور مملوکیت کے درمیان میں کتابت کی حالت تھی کہ کتابت اپنی ذات سے مملوکیت ہے اور اپنی کمائی اور تصرفات کی راہ سے آزادی ہے۔ پس جب نکاح اور طلاق کے درمیان ایسی حالت نہیں ہے تو جس نے نصف عورت کو طلاق دی تو یہ نصف طلاق کی وجہ سے حرام ہوا اور دوسرا نصف نکاح کی وجہ سے حلال ہوا اور اصول فقہ میں یہ قاعدہ مذکور ہے کہ اگر حلال و حرام جمع ہو جائیں تو حرام کو حلال پر ترجیح دے کر پوری عورت کو حرام قرار دیا جائے گا تا کہ احتیاط پر عمل ہو سکے۔ اسی طرح عفو میں ہے کہ جب آدھا قصاص معاف کیا ، تو معاف کر دینے کی وجہ سے یہ آدھا قصاص حرام ہو گیا اور دوسرا آدھا حلال ہے۔ پس حرام کو حلال پر ترجیح دے کر کہا جائے گا کہ پورا قصاص معاف ہو گیا اور اب قصاص لینا حرام ہے اور وہ استمیلاد پر قیاس کرنا تو یہ بھی صحیح نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ استیلاد یعنی ام ولد بنانا امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک متجری ہوتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ اعتاق متجری ہوتا ہے۔ حتی کہ اگر کسی مدبرہ باندی میں سے اپنے حصہ کوام ولد بنایا تو اسی حصہ تک رہے گا اور محض مملوکہ باندی میں ایسا ہوا ۔ تو جب اس نے اپنے شریک کو تاوان اس وجہ سے دے دیا کہ اس کی ملک فاسد کر دی ہے۔ تو تاوان دینے سے پوری باندی کا مالک ہو گیا۔ پس استیلا د بھی پورا ہو گیا۔
اس کی توضیح یہ ہے کہ زید و خالد کے درمیان ایک باندی مشترک ہے اور اس کے بچہ پیدا ہوا اور زید نے دعویٰ کیا کہ میرے نطفہ سے ہے تو آدھی باندی اس کی ام ولد ہو جائے گی۔ لیکن اس نے خالد کے حصہ میں فساد ڈال دیا۔ کیونکہ ام ولد بمنزلہ آزاد کے ہوتی ہے۔ حتی کہ اس کو بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے زید پر واجب ہوگا کہ خالد کے حصہ کا تاوان دے اور جب تاوان دے کر وہ پوری باندی کا مالک ہو گیا تو وہ باندی پوری اس کی ام ولد ہو جائے گی۔ جیسے کوئی اپنی خالص باندی استیلا د کرے۔ تو وہ پوری ام ولد ہو جاتی ہے اور اگر یہ مشتر کہ باندی دونوں کی مد برہ ہو یعنی دونوں نے کہا ہو کہ تو ہمارے مرنے کے بعد آزاد ہے۔ تو اس مسئلہ میں جس نے اس کے بچہ کا دعویٰ کیا ہے۔ اس کا حصہ ام ولد ر ہے گا اور باقی حصہ مد برہ رہے گا۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ استیلا د کے ٹکڑے ہو سکتے ہیں۔
(مینی)
غلام دو شر کا ء کے درمیان مشترک ہو ایک نے اپنے حصے کو آزاد کر دیا آزاد ہو
جائے گا دوسرے کے حصہ کا کیا ہوگا
و اذا كان العبد بين شريكين فاعتق احد هما نصيبه عتق فان كان موسر افشريكه بالخياران شاء اعتق وان شاء ضمن شريكه قيمة نصيبه وان شاء استسعى العبد فان ضمن رجع المعتق على العبد والولاء للمعتق وان اتق او استسعى فالو لاء بينهما وان كان المعتق معسرا فالشريك بالخيار ان شاء اعتق وان شاء استسعى العبد والولاء بينهما في الوجهين وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وقالا ليس له الا الضمان مع اليسار والسعاية مع الاعسارو لا يرجع المعتق على العبدو الولاء للمعتق
ترجمہ اور اگر ایک غلام دو شریکوں میں (مشترک) ہو۔ پس ان دونوں میں ایک نے اپنا حصہ آزد کیا۔ تو اس کا حصہ آزاد ہو جائے گا۔
Book of Emancipation. 307. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu... name is because ownership is the right of the emancipator and price is the right of Shariah. Because when the disbeliever denied being the slave of God, Allah punished him by making him a slave of His servant. Or servitude is the right of the general public. Because the mujahideen distribute goods other than slaves likewise they will distribute slaves. And the rule of disposition is only to the extent that the disposer has control, and that is that he removes his own right, not the right of another; i.e., the master can only remove ownership, not servitude, and ownership is divisible. Therefore emancipation is also divisible. And the reality is that disposition remains only where it is directed, and exceeding to other than that is only possible if it cannot be divided, and here ownership which is the master's right can be divided. As is evident in sale and gift: e.g., selling half a slave or gifting him is unanimously permissible. Therefore the disposition of emancipation will also remain on its original basis: i.e., if he frees half, it is permissible and only half becomes free. And the obligation of earning for the remaining portion upon the slave is because the value of the remaining portion remains with the slave, so it is to be collected from him. And the slave who is obligated to earn and pay is, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, like a mukatab. Because when emancipation is directed to a part of the slave, it necessarily follows, from the derivative, that he acquires ownership of his entire self, i.e., he becomes owner of his whole self. Because a free person is not divisible, and the remaining of the master's ownership in a part, due to servitude, requires that he not be owner of the whole self because servitude is also not divisible. The outcome is that two matters have combined: first, that the slave is not owner of his whole self; second, that the master's ownership remains in the slave's entire self. And since it is possible to act on both proofs, we have acted on both and made this slave... (broken) ... like a mukatab. Because a mukatab is owner of his earnings but not of his self. So similarly, this slave is owner of his earnings but not of his self. And when he is like a mukatab, his earnings are like the kitabah price. So the master has the option to collect the remaining value by making him earn, and also the option to free him if he wishes, because a mukatab is also eligible for the master to free him. But here is a question: if the mustas'a (earning slave) is in the rank of a mukatab, then just as a mukatab becomes a slave again if unable to pay the kitabah price, similarly the mustas'a should become a slave again if unable to earn, but that is not the case. When this slave, whose part has been freed and upon whom earning is made obligatory, becomes unable to earn, he cannot be called a slave again. The answer is that there is a difference between them: if a mukatab is unable to pay, he is enslaved again, but this slave, if unable to earn, cannot be enslaved. The reason for the difference is that freeing a slave is an isqat la ila ahad (suspension of ownership to no one), i.e., it removes ownership to no one, and isqat la ila ahad has no meaning of exchange because exchange occurs between two persons, and here there is only one person, the emancipator. So when the meaning of exchange is not found in this case, it is not subject to revocation. In contrast, kitabah: when a transaction is made with the slave, it is an isqat from the master to the mukatab, in that the master gave the mukatab the ability to acquire the kitabah price. Therefore, in kitabah the meaning of exchange exists, and when the meaning of exchange exists, kitabah can be rescinded (iqalah) or annulled (faskh). [Page 309] Book of Emancipation. 308. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidayah Volume 2. 'Wa laysa fi al-talaq...' etc. is the answer to the qiyas of the two Sahibayn and Imam Shafi'i that it is like talaq, forgiveness of qisas, and istilad. Thus he said: Qiyas of emancipation to talaq and forgiveness of qisas is not correct because there is no intermediate state between talaq and marriage or between qisas and forgiveness. Just as there was the state of kitabah between freedom and servitude, because kitabah is servitude in essence and freedom through earnings and dispositions. So when there is no such state between marriage and talaq, then if one gives half talaq to a woman, that half becomes forbidden due to talaq and the other half remains permitted due to marriage, and the usul al-fiqh rule is that if halal and haram combine, then preference is given to haram over halal, declaring the whole woman forbidden in order to act on precaution. Similarly in forgiveness: when half of the qisas is forgiven, that half becomes forbidden due to forgiveness, and the other half remains permissible. So preference is given to haram, and it is said that the entire qisas is forgiven and taking qisas is now forbidden. And qiyas to istilad is also not correct because istilad (making an umm walad) according to Imam Abu Hanifa is divisible, just as emancipation is divisible. Even if one makes his share of a mudabbara slave-girl an umm walad, it is confined to that share. In a purely owned slave-girl, when he gave compensation to his partner because he invalidated his ownership, then by giving compensation he became the owner of the whole slave-girl, so the istilad becomes complete as well. Its explanation: Zaid and Khalid jointly own a slave-girl, and she gives birth, and Zaid claims paternity; then half the slave-girl becomes his umm walad. But he caused defect in Khalid's share because an umm walad is like a free person, to the extent that selling her is not permissible. So Zaid must pay compensation for Khalid's share, and when he pays compensation and becomes the owner of the whole slave-girl, the entire slave-girl becomes his umm walad, just as if one makes his own exclusive slave-girl an umm walad, then she becomes fully umm walad. And if this jointly owned slave-girl is mudabbara by both (i.e., both said she is free after their death), then in this case the one who claims the child, his share becomes umm walad and the remaining share remains mudabbara. So it is established that istilad can be divided. (Matn) A slave jointly owned between two partners: one partner freed his share, it becomes free. What about the other's share? And if a slave is between two partners and one of them frees his share, his share is freed. If the freeing person is wealthy, his partner has the option: if he wishes, he may free (the remaining share); if he wishes, he may claim from his partner the value of his share; if he wishes, he may make the slave earn. If he claims compensation, the freeing person recovers from the slave, and the wala' belongs to the freeing person. If he frees or makes the slave earn, the wala' is between them. If the freeing person is poor, the partner has the option: if he wishes, he may free; if he wishes, he may make the slave earn. In both cases, the wala' is between them. This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two Sahibayn said: He (the partner) has only the option of compensation (if wealthy) or earning (if poor), and the freeing person does not recover from the slave, and the wala' is for the freeing person. Translation: And if a slave is jointly owned between two partners, and one of them freed his share, then his share is freed.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Bidayah is a commentary on the Hidayah, addressing the rulings of partial emancipation of a jointly owned slave. It begins by establishing that ownership is divisible, so emancipation (like sale) can be partial. When one partner frees his share, that share becomes free. The remaining share's value must be compensated by the slave through earnings (istis'a') because the slave now has a degree of freedom akin to a mukatab (a slave under contract of emancipation). The proof for this is istihsan, preferring equity over strict analogy (qiyas). The commentator then refutes the analogy that would equate partial emancipation to partial divorce (talaq) or partial forgiveness of qisas, where the rule of 'if halal and haram combine, prefer haram' applies. The difference is that in emancipation there is an intermediate state (the slave being partially free) similar to kitabah, whereas in divorce and qisas there is no such intermediate state. Similarly, the analogy to istilad (making a slave-girl an umm walad) is refuted because, according to Abu Hanifa, istilad is also divisible. The passage concludes with the matn (core text) stating the ruling of Abu Hanifa and the disagreement of the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). Abu Hanifa gives the partner three options when the freeing person is wealthy: free the remaining share, take compensation from the freeing person, or make the slave earn. If the freeing person is poor, the partner has two options: free or make the slave earn. In contrast, the Sahibayn restrict the partner to only compensation (if wealthy) or earning (if poor), and the freeing person does not recoup compensation from the slave, and the wala' (patronage) belongs solely to the freeing person. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa, as it is the basis for fatwa in most later works.

Key Terms
عتق ('itq): Emancipation of a slave; the act of freeing a slave from bondage.
مستسعى (mustas'a): A slave who is obligated to earn and pay the value of the remaining unfreed portion to the master.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave under a contract of emancipation (kitabah) who pays installments to his master to earn freedom.
إسقاط لا إلى أحد (isqat la ila ahad): Suspension or removal of a right without transferring it to another person. Used here to describe the nature of emancipation as a pure relinquishment of ownership.
استحسان (istihsan): Equitable preference in law, preferring a ruling based on a stronger analogy or need over a weaker analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a partner frees his share in a jointly owned slave and is wealthy, what is NOT an option for the other partner?
A) Free the remaining share
B) Claim compensation from the freeing partner
C) Make the slave earn the value of the remaining share
D) Demand the freeing partner free the entire slave

Key Takeaway
Partial emancipation is valid; the partner has specific options depending on the freeer's wealth, and wala' consequences vary accordingly.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn on Partner's Options
Intra-Hanafi dispute on partner's options

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the partner's options in partial emancipation, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa gives the partner three options; the Sahibayn restrict to only compensation or istis'a', and wala' goes to the freeer alone.

Within the Hanafi school, there is an important dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two principal disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), regarding the partner's options when one co-owner frees his share in a jointly owned slave. This lesson focuses on that disagreement, the proofs on each side, and the practical difference in rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the disputed issue
The issue is: what options does the partner have when one partner frees his share in a jointly owned slave?
The dispute is only about the options; both agree the freed share becomes free.
2
Outline Abu Hanifa's view
Abu Hanifa: If the freeer is wealthy, partner may free, take compensation, or make the slave earn (istis'a'). If poor, partner may free or make the slave earn. Wala' is shared if partner frees or uses istis'a'; if compensation, wala' for freeer alone.
This is the matn's position.
3
Outline the Sahibayn's view
Sahibayn: If the freeer is wealthy, partner may only claim compensation; if poor, only make the slave earn. No option to free the remaining share. Wala' always goes to the freeer alone.
The freeer does not recoup from the slave.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Under Abu Hanifa, the partner can free the remaining share and share wala'. Under Sahibayn, the partner cannot free and loses any share in wala'.
This affects the partner's incentive and the distribution of patronage.
5
State the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa, as held by most later Hanafi authorities.
Al-Marghinani and others prefer Abu Hanifa's view.

اشرف البدایہ شرح ار به يه - بعد تنم ار... نام ہے کیونکہ ملک آزاد کرنے والے کا حق ہے اور قیمت شریعت کا حق ہے۔ کیونکہ کا فر نے جب عبد اللہ ، خدا کا غلام ہونے سے انکار کیا تو اللہ نے اس کو اس طرح بدلہ دیا کہ اپنے بندے کا غلام بنایا۔ یا رقیت عام لوگوں کا حق ہے۔ کیونکہ مجاہد بین جس طرح رقیق کے علاوہ سامان کو تقسیم کرتے ہیں اسی طرح رقیق بھی تقسیم کریں گے اور تصرف کا حکم اس قدر ہوتا ہے جتنا کہ تصرف کرنے والے کے قابو میں ہے اور وہ یہی ہے کہ اپنا حق دور کرے، نہ کہ غیر کا حق یعنی مولی صرف ملک دور کر سکتا ہے نہ کہ رقیت اور ملک متجری ہے۔ لہذا اعتاق بھی متجری ہوگا اور بات دراصل یہ ہے کہ تصرف اسی جگہ تک رہتا ہے۔ جہاں اسکی نسبت کی گئی ہو اور اس جگہ سے علاوہ کی طرف تجاوز کرنا اسی ضرورت سے ہو سکتا ہے کہ اس کی تجربی نہ ہو سکے اور یہاں ملک جو مولی کا حق ہے اسکی تجزی ہو سکتی ہے۔ جیسے بیع اور بیہ میں ظاہر ہے یعنی مثلاً آدھا غلام بیچا یا ہبہ کیا، تو بالا تفاق جائز ہے۔ پس اعتناق کا تصرف بھی اپنی اصل پر رہے گا۔ یعنی اگر آدھا آزاد کیا تو جائز ہے۔ آدھا ہی آزاد ہوگا۔

مال سے عاجز ہو تو وہ رقیق کر دیا جاتا ہے اور یہ غلام اگر کمائی سے عاجز ہو جائے تو رقیق نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔ وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ غلام آزاد کرنا اسقاط لا الی احد ہے۔ یعنی اس سے ملکیت ساقط کر نالا الی احد ہے اور اسقاط لا الی احد میں معاوضہ کے معنی نہیں پائے جاتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ معاوضہ دو آدمیوں کے درمیان متحقق ہوتا ہے اور یہاں صرف ایک آدمی ہے یعنی آزاد کرنے والا ۔ پس جب اس صورت میں معاوضہ کے معنی نہیں پائے گئے تو یہ نسخ کے قابل بھی نہیں ہے۔

وليس في الطلاق ... الخ سے صاحبین اور امام شافعی کے قیاس فصار کا لطلاق والعفو عن القصاص والاستمیلاد کا جواب ہے۔ چنانچہ فرمایا کہ اعتناق کو طلاق اور عفو عن القصاص پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ طلاق اور نکاح کے درمیان یا قصاص اور محفو کے درمیان کوئی درمیانی حالت نہیں ہے۔ جیسا آزادی اور مملوکیت کے درمیان میں کتابت کی حالت تھی کہ کتابت اپنی ذات سے مملوکیت ہے اور اپنی کمائی اور تصرفات کی راہ سے آزادی ہے۔ پس جب نکاح اور طلاق کے درمیان ایسی حالت نہیں ہے تو جس نے نصف عورت کو طلاق دی تو یہ نصف طلاق کی وجہ سے حرام ہوا اور دوسرا نصف نکاح کی وجہ سے حلال ہوا اور اصول فقہ میں یہ قاعدہ مذکور ہے کہ اگر حلال و حرام جمع ہو جائیں تو حرام کو حلال پر ترجیح دے کر پوری عورت کو حرام قرار دیا جائے گا تا کہ احتیاط پر عمل ہو سکے۔ اسی طرح عفو میں ہے کہ جب آدھا قصاص معاف کیا ، تو معاف کر دینے کی وجہ سے یہ آدھا قصاص حرام ہو گیا اور دوسرا آدھا حلال ہے۔ پس حرام کو حلال پر ترجیح دے کر کہا جائے گا کہ پورا قصاص معاف ہو گیا اور اب قصاص لینا حرام ہے اور وہ استمیلاد پر قیاس کرنا تو یہ بھی صحیح نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ استیلاد یعنی ام ولد بنانا امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک متجری ہوتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ اعتاق متجری ہوتا ہے۔ حتی کہ اگر کسی مدبرہ باندی میں سے اپنے حصہ کوام ولد بنایا تو اسی حصہ تک رہے گا اور محض مملوکہ باندی میں ایسا ہوا ۔ تو جب اس نے اپنے شریک کو تاوان اس وجہ سے دے دیا کہ اس کی ملک فاسد کر دی ہے۔ تو تاوان دینے سے پوری باندی کا مالک ہو گیا۔ پس استیلا د بھی پورا ہو گیا۔
اس کی توضیح یہ ہے کہ زید و خالد کے درمیان ایک باندی مشترک ہے اور اس کے بچہ پیدا ہوا اور زید نے دعویٰ کیا کہ میرے نطفہ سے ہے تو آدھی باندی اس کی ام ولد ہو جائے گی۔ لیکن اس نے خالد کے حصہ میں فساد ڈال دیا۔ کیونکہ ام ولد بمنزلہ آزاد کے ہوتی ہے۔ حتی کہ اس کو بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے زید پر واجب ہوگا کہ خالد کے حصہ کا تاوان دے اور جب تاوان دے کر وہ پوری باندی کا مالک ہو گیا تو وہ باندی پوری اس کی ام ولد ہو جائے گی۔ جیسے کوئی اپنی خالص باندی استیلا د کرے۔ تو وہ پوری ام ولد ہو جاتی ہے اور اگر یہ مشتر کہ باندی دونوں کی مد برہ ہو یعنی دونوں نے کہا ہو کہ تو ہمارے مرنے کے بعد آزاد ہے۔ تو اس مسئلہ میں جس نے اس کے بچہ کا دعویٰ کیا ہے۔ اس کا حصہ ام ولد ر ہے گا اور باقی حصہ مد برہ رہے گا۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ استیلا د کے ٹکڑے ہو سکتے ہیں۔
(مینی)

و اذا كان العبد بين شريكين فاعتق احد هما نصيبه عتق فان كان موسر افشريكه بالخياران شاء اعتق وان شاء ضمن شريكه قيمة نصيبه وان شاء استسعى العبد فان ضمن رجع المعتق على العبد والولاء للمعتق وان اتق او استسعى فالو لاء بينهما وان كان المعتق معسرا فالشريك بالخيار ان شاء اعتق وان شاء استسعى العبد والولاء بينهما في الوجهين وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وقالا ليس له الا الضمان مع اليسار والسعاية مع الاعسارو لا يرجع المعتق على العبدو الولاء للمعتق
ترجمہ اور اگر ایک غلام دو شریکوں میں (مشترک) ہو۔ پس ان دونوں میں ایک نے اپنا حصہ آزد کیا۔ تو اس کا حصہ آزاد ہو جائے گا۔
Book of Emancipation. 307. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu... name is because ownership is the right of the emancipator and price is the right of Shariah. Because when the disbeliever denied being the slave of God, Allah punished him by making him a slave of His servant. Or servitude is the right of the general public. Because the mujahideen distribute goods other than slaves likewise they will distribute slaves. And the rule of disposition is only to the extent that the disposer has control, and that is that he removes his own right, not the right of another; i.e., the master can only remove ownership, not servitude, and ownership is divisible. Therefore emancipation is also divisible. And the reality is that disposition remains only where it is directed, and exceeding to other than that is only possible if it cannot be divided, and here ownership which is the master's right can be divided. As is evident in sale and gift: e.g., selling half a slave or gifting him is unanimously permissible. Therefore the disposition of emancipation will also remain on its original basis: i.e., if he frees half, it is permissible and only half becomes free. And the obligation of earning for the remaining portion upon the slave is because the value of the remaining portion remains with the slave, so it is to be collected from him. And the slave who is obligated to earn and pay is, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, like a mukatab. Because when emancipation is directed to a part of the slave, it necessarily follows, from the derivative, that he acquires ownership of his entire self, i.e., he becomes owner of his whole self. Because a free person is not divisible, and the remaining of the master's ownership in a part, due to servitude, requires that he not be owner of the whole self because servitude is also not divisible. The outcome is that two matters have combined: first, that the slave is not owner of his whole self; second, that the master's ownership remains in the slave's entire self. And since it is possible to act on both proofs, we have acted on both and made this slave... (broken) ... like a mukatab. Because a mukatab is owner of his earnings but not of his self. So similarly, this slave is owner of his earnings but not of his self. And when he is like a mukatab, his earnings are like the kitabah price. So the master has the option to collect the remaining value by making him earn, and also the option to free him if he wishes, because a mukatab is also eligible for the master to free him. But here is a question: if the mustas'a (earning slave) is in the rank of a mukatab, then just as a mukatab becomes a slave again if unable to pay the kitabah price, similarly the mustas'a should become a slave again if unable to earn, but that is not the case. When this slave, whose part has been freed and upon whom earning is made obligatory, becomes unable to earn, he cannot be called a slave again. The answer is that there is a difference between them: if a mukatab is unable to pay, he is enslaved again, but this slave, if unable to earn, cannot be enslaved. The reason for the difference is that freeing a slave is an isqat la ila ahad (suspension of ownership to no one), i.e., it removes ownership to no one, and isqat la ila ahad has no meaning of exchange because exchange occurs between two persons, and here there is only one person, the emancipator. So when the meaning of exchange is not found in this case, it is not subject to revocation. In contrast, kitabah: when a transaction is made with the slave, it is an isqat from the master to the mukatab, in that the master gave the mukatab the ability to acquire the kitabah price. Therefore, in kitabah the meaning of exchange exists, and when the meaning of exchange exists, kitabah can be rescinded (iqalah) or annulled (faskh). [Page 309] Book of Emancipation. 308. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidayah Volume 2. 'Wa laysa fi al-talaq...' etc. is the answer to the qiyas of the two Sahibayn and Imam Shafi'i that it is like talaq, forgiveness of qisas, and istilad. Thus he said: Qiyas of emancipation to talaq and forgiveness of qisas is not correct because there is no intermediate state between talaq and marriage or between qisas and forgiveness. Just as there was the state of kitabah between freedom and servitude, because kitabah is servitude in essence and freedom through earnings and dispositions. So when there is no such state between marriage and talaq, then if one gives half talaq to a woman, that half becomes forbidden due to talaq and the other half remains permitted due to marriage, and the usul al-fiqh rule is that if halal and haram combine, then preference is given to haram over halal, declaring the whole woman forbidden in order to act on precaution. Similarly in forgiveness: when half of the qisas is forgiven, that half becomes forbidden due to forgiveness, and the other half remains permissible. So preference is given to haram, and it is said that the entire qisas is forgiven and taking qisas is now forbidden. And qiyas to istilad is also not correct because istilad (making an umm walad) according to Imam Abu Hanifa is divisible, just as emancipation is divisible. Even if one makes his share of a mudabbara slave-girl an umm walad, it is confined to that share. In a purely owned slave-girl, when he gave compensation to his partner because he invalidated his ownership, then by giving compensation he became the owner of the whole slave-girl, so the istilad becomes complete as well. Its explanation: Zaid and Khalid jointly own a slave-girl, and she gives birth, and Zaid claims paternity; then half the slave-girl becomes his umm walad. But he caused defect in Khalid's share because an umm walad is like a free person, to the extent that selling her is not permissible. So Zaid must pay compensation for Khalid's share, and when he pays compensation and becomes the owner of the whole slave-girl, the entire slave-girl becomes his umm walad, just as if one makes his own exclusive slave-girl an umm walad, then she becomes fully umm walad. And if this jointly owned slave-girl is mudabbara by both (i.e., both said she is free after their death), then in this case the one who claims the child, his share becomes umm walad and the remaining share remains mudabbara. So it is established that istilad can be divided. (Matn) A slave jointly owned between two partners: one partner freed his share, it becomes free. What about the other's share? And if a slave is between two partners and one of them frees his share, his share is freed. If the freeing person is wealthy, his partner has the option: if he wishes, he may free (the remaining share); if he wishes, he may claim from his partner the value of his share; if he wishes, he may make the slave earn. If he claims compensation, the freeing person recovers from the slave, and the wala' belongs to the freeing person. If he frees or makes the slave earn, the wala' is between them. If the freeing person is poor, the partner has the option: if he wishes, he may free; if he wishes, he may make the slave earn. In both cases, the wala' is between them. This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two Sahibayn said: He (the partner) has only the option of compensation (if wealthy) or earning (if poor), and the freeing person does not recover from the slave, and the wala' is for the freeing person. Translation: And if a slave is jointly owned between two partners, and one of them freed his share, then his share is freed.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Bidayah is a commentary on the Hidayah, addressing the rulings of partial emancipation of a jointly owned slave. It begins by establishing that ownership is divisible, so emancipation (like sale) can be partial. When one partner frees his share, that share becomes free. The remaining share's value must be compensated by the slave through earnings (istis'a') because the slave now has a degree of freedom akin to a mukatab (a slave under contract of emancipation). The proof for this is istihsan, preferring equity over strict analogy (qiyas). The commentator then refutes the analogy that would equate partial emancipation to partial divorce (talaq) or partial forgiveness of qisas, where the rule of 'if halal and haram combine, prefer haram' applies. The difference is that in emancipation there is an intermediate state (the slave being partially free) similar to kitabah, whereas in divorce and qisas there is no such intermediate state. Similarly, the analogy to istilad (making a slave-girl an umm walad) is refuted because, according to Abu Hanifa, istilad is also divisible. The passage concludes with the matn (core text) stating the ruling of Abu Hanifa and the disagreement of the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). Abu Hanifa gives the partner three options when the freeing person is wealthy: free the remaining share, take compensation from the freeing person, or make the slave earn. If the freeing person is poor, the partner has two options: free or make the slave earn. In contrast, the Sahibayn restrict the partner to only compensation (if wealthy) or earning (if poor), and the freeing person does not recoup compensation from the slave, and the wala' (patronage) belongs solely to the freeing person. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa, as it is the basis for fatwa in most later works.

Key Terms
عتق ('itq): Emancipation of a slave; the act of freeing a slave from bondage.
مستسعى (mustas'a): A slave who is obligated to earn and pay the value of the remaining unfreed portion to the master.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave under a contract of emancipation (kitabah) who pays installments to his master to earn freedom.
إسقاط لا إلى أحد (isqat la ila ahad): Suspension or removal of a right without transferring it to another person. Used here to describe the nature of emancipation as a pure relinquishment of ownership.
استحسان (istihsan): Equitable preference in law, preferring a ruling based on a stronger analogy or need over a weaker analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, what is the partner's only option when the freeing partner is wealthy?
A) Free the remaining share
B) Claim compensation from the freeing partner
C) Make the slave earn
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on partner's options revolves around whether the partner can free the remaining share; Abu Hanifa permits it, Sahibayn restrict it, and the mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa.

12 min
Proof and Refutation: Istihsan vs. Qiyas in Partial Emancipation
Proof and refutation of qiyas in partial emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school uses istihsan to validate partial emancipation, and refute the qiyas to talaq and qisas.

Core Idea
Istihsan overrides qiyas because emancipation allows an intermediate state (like kitabah), which does not exist in divorce or qisas.

The proof for the validity of partial emancipation and the partner's options is based on istihsan (equitable preference). The opposing view, held by the Sahibayn and the Shafi'i school, uses qiyas to talaq (divorce) and forgiveness of qisas (retaliation). This lesson dissects that qiyas, explains why it fails according to Abu Hanifa, and shows how istihsan provides a sounder basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opposing qiyas
Sahibayn and Imam Shafi'i analogize partial emancipation to partial divorce and partial forgiveness of qisas. In those cases, when halal and haram combine, the rule 'prefer haram' applies, making the entire act haram.
In divorce, half talaq makes the whole woman forbidden; in qisas, half forgiveness extinguishes the entire qisas.
2
State the rule of combining halal and haram
The usul al-fiqh rule: if halal and haram combine, haram is preferred (yufaddal al-haram) to act with precaution. This forces the entire thing to be considered haram.
This rule applies when there is no intermediate state.
3
Explain the Hanafi objection: intermediate state exists
Emancipation has an intermediate state: the slave becomes partially free, similar to a mukatab (a slave under contract). In divorce and qisas, no such intermediate state exists; a woman is either married or divorced, a life is either subject to qisas or forgiven.
The existence of an intermediate state prevents the application of the 'prefer haram' rule.
4
Support with istihsan
Istihsan prefers the ruling that is more equitable and recognizes the divisible nature of ownership. Since ownership can be divided, emancipation can be partial. This is stronger than the qiyas based on a false analogy.
Istihsan is a primary source in the Hanafi school.
5
Conclude with the correct ruling
Thus, partial emancipation is valid, the freed share becomes free, and the partner has the options as per Abu Hanifa. The qiyas to talaq and qisas is rejected because of the distinguishing feature (farq) of the intermediate state.

مال سے عاجز ہو تو وہ رقیق کر دیا جاتا ہے اور یہ غلام اگر کمائی سے عاجز ہو جائے تو رقیق نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔ وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ غلام آزاد کرنا اسقاط لا الی احد ہے۔ یعنی اس سے ملکیت ساقط کر نالا الی احد ہے گئے تو یہ نسخ کے قابل بھی نہیں ہے۔

اس کی توضیح یہ ہے کہ زید و خالد کے درمیان ایک باندی مشترک ہے اور اس کے بچہ پیدا ہوا اور زید نے دعویٰ کیا کہ میرے نطفہ سے ہے تو آدھی باندی اس کی ام ولد ہو جائے گی۔ لیکن اس نے خالد کے حصہ میں فساد ڈال دیا۔ کیونکہ ام ولد بمنزلہ آزاد کے ہوتی ہے۔ حتی کہ اس کو بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے زید پر واجب ہوگا کہ خالد کے حصہ کا تاوان دے اور جب تاوان دے کر وہ پوری باندی کا مالک ہو گیا تو وہ باندی پوری اس کی ام ولد ہو جائے گی۔ جیسے کوئی اپنی خالص باندی استیلا د کرے۔ تو وہ پوری ام ولد ہو جاتی ہے اور اگر یہ مشتر کہ باندی دونوں کی مد برہ ہو یعنی دونوں نے کہا ہو کہ تو ہمارے مرنے کے بعد آزاد ہے۔ تو اس مسئلہ میں جس نے اس کے بچہ کا دعویٰ کیا ہے۔ اس کا حصہ ام ولد ر ہے گا اور باقی حصہ مد برہ رہے گا۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ استیلا د کے ٹکڑے ہو سکتے ہیں۔
(مینی)
غلام دو شر کا ء کے درمیان مشترک ہو ایک نے اپنے حصے کو آزاد کر دیا آزاد ہو

و اذا كان العبد بين شريكين فاعتق احد هما نصيبه عتق فان كان موسر افشريكه بالخياران شاء اعتق وان شاء ضمن شريكه قيمة نصيبه وان شاء استسعى العبد فان ضمن رجع المعتق على العبد والولاء للمعتق وان اتق او استسعى فالو لاء بينهما وان كان المعتق معسرا فالشريك بالخيار ان شاء اعتق وان شاء استسعى العبد والولاء بينهما في الوجهين وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وقالا ليس له الا الضمان مع اليسار والسعاية مع الاعسارو لا يرجع المعتق على العبدو الولاء للمعتق
ترجمہ اور اگر ایک غلام دو شریکوں میں (مشترک) ہو۔ پس ان دونوں میں ایک نے اپنا حصہ آزد کیا۔ تو اس کا حصہ آزاد ہو جائے گا۔
Book of Emancipation. 307. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu... name is because ownership is the right of the emancipator and price is the right of Shariah. Because when the disbeliever denied being the slave of God, Allah punished him by making him a slave of His servant. Or servitude is the right of the general public. Because the mujahideen distribute goods other than slaves likewise they will distribute slaves. And the rule of disposition is only to the extent that the disposer has control, and that is that he removes his own right, not the right of another; i.e., the master can only remove ownership, not servitude, and ownership is divisible. Therefore emancipation is also divisible. And the reality is that disposition remains only where it is directed, and exceeding to other than that is only possible if it cannot be divided, and here ownership which is the master's right can be divided. As is evident in sale and gift: e.g., selling half a slave or gifting him is unanimously permissible. Therefore the disposition of emancipation will also remain on its original basis: i.e., if he frees half, it is permissible and only half becomes free. And the obligation of earning for the remaining portion upon the slave is because the value of the remaining portion remains with the slave, so it is to be collected from him. And the slave who is obligated to earn and pay is, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, like a mukatab. Because when emancipation is directed to a part of the slave, it necessarily follows, from the derivative, that he acquires ownership of his entire self, i.e., he becomes owner of his whole self. Because a free person is not divisible, and the remaining of the master's ownership in a part, due to servitude, requires that he not be owner of the whole self because servitude is also not divisible. The outcome is that two matters have combined: first, that the slave is not owner of his whole self; second, that the master's ownership remains in the slave's entire self. And since it is possible to act on both proofs, we have acted on both and made this slave... (broken) ... like a mukatab. Because a mukatab is owner of his earnings but not of his self. So similarly, this slave is owner of his earnings but not of his self. And when he is like a mukatab, his earnings are like the kitabah price. So the master has the option to collect the remaining value by making him earn, and also the option to free him if he wishes, because a mukatab is also eligible for the master to free him. But here is a question: if the mustas'a (earning slave) is in the rank of a mukatab, then just as a mukatab becomes a slave again if unable to pay the kitabah price, similarly the mustas'a should become a slave again if unable to earn, but that is not the case. When this slave, whose part has been freed and upon whom earning is made obligatory, becomes unable to earn, he cannot be called a slave again. The answer is that there is a difference between them: if a mukatab is unable to pay, he is enslaved again, but this slave, if unable to earn, cannot be enslaved. The reason for the difference is that freeing a slave is an isqat la ila ahad (suspension of ownership to no one), i.e., it removes ownership to no one, and isqat la ila ahad has no meaning of exchange because exchange occurs between two persons, and here there is only one person, the emancipator. So when the meaning of exchange is not found in this case, it is not subject to revocation. In contrast, kitabah: when a transaction is made with the slave, it is an isqat from the master to the mukatab, in that the master gave the mukatab the ability to acquire the kitabah price. Therefore, in kitabah the meaning of exchange exists, and when the meaning of exchange exists, kitabah can be rescinded (iqalah) or annulled (faskh). [Page 309] Book of Emancipation. 308. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidayah Volume 2. 'Wa laysa fi al-talaq...' etc. is the answer to the qiyas of the two Sahibayn and Imam Shafi'i that it is like talaq, forgiveness of qisas, and istilad. Thus he said: Qiyas of emancipation to talaq and forgiveness of qisas is not correct because there is no intermediate state between talaq and marriage or between qisas and forgiveness. Just as there was the state of kitabah between freedom and servitude, because kitabah is servitude in essence and freedom through earnings and dispositions. So when there is no such state between marriage and talaq, then if one gives half talaq to a woman, that half becomes forbidden due to talaq and the other half remains permitted due to marriage, and the usul al-fiqh rule is that if halal and haram combine, then preference is given to haram over halal, declaring the whole woman forbidden in order to act on precaution. Similarly in forgiveness: when half of the qisas is forgiven, that half becomes forbidden due to forgiveness, and the other half remains permissible. So preference is given to haram, and it is said that the entire qisas is forgiven and taking qisas is now forbidden. And qiyas to istilad is also not correct because istilad (making an umm walad) according to Imam Abu Hanifa is divisible, just as emancipation is divisible. Even if one makes his share of a mudabbara slave-girl an umm walad, it is confined to that share. In a purely owned slave-girl, when he gave compensation to his partner because he invalidated his ownership, then by giving compensation he became the owner of the whole slave-girl, so the istilad becomes complete as well. Its explanation: Zaid and Khalid jointly own a slave-girl, and she gives birth, and Zaid claims paternity; then half the slave-girl becomes his umm walad. But he caused defect in Khalid's share because an umm walad is like a free person, to the extent that selling her is not permissible. So Zaid must pay compensation for Khalid's share, and when he pays compensation and becomes the owner of the whole slave-girl, the entire slave-girl becomes his umm walad, just as if one makes his own exclusive slave-girl an umm walad, then she becomes fully umm walad. And if this jointly owned slave-girl is mudabbara by both (i.e., both said she is free after their death), then in this case the one who claims the child, his share becomes umm walad and the remaining share remains mudabbara. So it is established that istilad can be divided. (Matn) A slave jointly owned between two partners: one partner freed his share, it becomes free. What about the other's share? And if a slave is between two partners and one of them frees his share, his share is freed. If the freeing person is wealthy, his partner has the option: if he wishes, he may free (the remaining share); if he wishes, he may claim from his partner the value of his share; if he wishes, he may make the slave earn. If he claims compensation, the freeing person recovers from the slave, and the wala' belongs to the freeing person. If he frees or makes the slave earn, the wala' is between them. If the freeing person is poor, the partner has the option: if he wishes, he may free; if he wishes, he may make the slave earn. In both cases, the wala' is between them. This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two Sahibayn said: He (the partner) has only the option of compensation (if wealthy) or earning (if poor), and the freeing person does not recover from the slave, and the wala' is for the freeing person. Translation: And if a slave is jointly owned between two partners, and one of them freed his share, then his share is freed.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Bidayah is a commentary on the Hidayah, addressing the rulings of partial emancipation of a jointly owned slave. It begins by establishing that ownership is divisible, so emancipation (like sale) can be partial. When one partner frees his share, that share becomes free. The remaining share's value must be compensated by the slave through earnings (istis'a') because the slave now has a degree of freedom akin to a mukatab (a slave under contract of emancipation). The proof for this is istihsan, preferring equity over strict analogy (qiyas). The commentator then refutes the analogy that would equate partial emancipation to partial divorce (talaq) or partial forgiveness of qisas, where the rule of 'if halal and haram combine, prefer haram' applies. The difference is that in emancipation there is an intermediate state (the slave being partially free) similar to kitabah, whereas in divorce and qisas there is no such intermediate state. Similarly, the analogy to istilad (making a slave-girl an umm walad) is refuted because, according to Abu Hanifa, istilad is also divisible. The passage concludes with the matn (core text) stating the ruling of Abu Hanifa and the disagreement of the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). Abu Hanifa gives the partner three options when the freeing person is wealthy: free the remaining share, take compensation from the freeing person, or make the slave earn. If the freeing person is poor, the partner has two options: free or make the slave earn. In contrast, the Sahibayn restrict the partner to only compensation (if wealthy) or earning (if poor), and the freeing person does not recoup compensation from the slave, and the wala' (patronage) belongs solely to the freeing person. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa, as it is the basis for fatwa in most later works.

Key Terms
عتق ('itq): Emancipation of a slave; the act of freeing a slave from bondage.
مستسعى (mustas'a): A slave who is obligated to earn and pay the value of the remaining unfreed portion to the master.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave under a contract of emancipation (kitabah) who pays installments to his master to earn freedom.
إسقاط لا إلى أحد (isqat la ila ahad): Suspension or removal of a right without transferring it to another person. Used here to describe the nature of emancipation as a pure relinquishment of ownership.
استحسان (istihsan): Equitable preference in law, preferring a ruling based on a stronger analogy or need over a weaker analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key reason the Hanafi school rejects the qiyas of partial emancipation to partial divorce?
A) Because divorce is a stronger act than emancipation
B) Because emancipation has an intermediate state (partial freedom) that divorce lacks
C) Because the Quran explicitly prohibits qiyas in emancipation
D) Because the Sahibayn's view is not authoritative

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses istihsan to validate partial emancipation, overriding the qiyas to talaq and qisas because emancipation has an intermediate state (partial freedom) that those cases lack.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Recoupment from Slave When Co-Owner Frees His Share
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the conditions for requiring the slave to work after partial emancipation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding a co-owner's right to reclaim from the slave after freeing his share, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The Sahibayn's view (mufta bihi) holds that a wealthy freeing co-owner cannot reclaim from the slave; only a poor one can require sa'yah.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the consequences of a co-owner freeing his share of a jointly-owned slave. The central question is whether the freeing co-owner, after compensating the silent partner, can demand repayment from the slave. The disagreement hinges on two foundational principles: the divisibility of emancipation and the effect of the freeing master's wealth on the slave's obligation to work (sa'yah). Let us dissect the arguments and identify the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether the freeing master can reclaim from the slave.
Abu Hanifa allows reclaim; Sahibayn restrict it based on wealth.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
Examine the Sahibayn's proof: the hadith from Abu Hurairah that distinguishes between wealthy and poor freeing masters.
Hadith: 'If he is wealthy... if he is poor...'
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Analyze the Sahibayn's use of the hadith and their abandonment of conflicting analogies (qiyas).
They dismiss two contradictory qiyas and rely on the explicit text.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand Abu Hanifa's counter-argument: the hadith is conditional; it does not forbid sa'yah in wealth. Also, his analogy to the cloth and dye case.
Conditionality does not imply negation in the absence of the condition.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Identify the practical consequences: when does the slave have to work? And which view is relied upon for fatwa?
Mufta bihi: Sahibayn's view - wealthy master cannot reclaim; poor master requires sa'yah.

تشریح صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ یہ مسئلہ یعنی آزاد کرنے والے کا اپنے شریک کو منمان ادا کرنے کے بعد غلام سے واپس لینا یا نہ لینا دو اصلوں پر مبنی ہے۔ اصل اول یہ ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اعتاق کے ٹکڑے ہو سکتے ہیں۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اعتاق کے ٹکڑے نہیں ہو سکتے۔ جیسا کہ ہم اول باب میں بیان کر چکے اور اصل دوم یہ ہے کہ جب آزاد کرنے والا خوشحال ہو تو اس کی ہم شمالی امام کے [؟] کے نزدیک غلام کی کمائی کرنے سے مانع نہیں ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک مانع ہے۔ اصل اول کے دلائل سابق میں گذر چکے۔ اور اصل دوم میں صاحبین کی دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اس مسئلہ میں قیاس کا مشخصی دو امروں میں سے ایک ہے۔ ایک تو یہ آزاد کرنے والا مالدار ہو یا تنگدست ۔ دونوں صورتوں میں آزاد کرنے والے پر اپنے شریک کے واسطے ضمان و باب ہو ہ ۔ کیونکہ اس نے اپنے حصہ کو آزاد کرنے کی وجہ سے اپنے شریک کے حصہ کو خراب کر ڈالا ۔ اسلئے کہ اس کے واسطے اپنی ملک کو برقرار رکھنا اور اپنے حصہ میں تصرف کرنا متعذر ہو گیا ہے اور ضمان افساد مالداری اور مفلسی کی وجہ سے مختلف نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ دوسرا امریہ کہ آزاد کر نے والے پر بالکل ضمان واجب نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ آزاد کرنے والے نے اپنے حصہ میں تصرف کیا ہے اور اپنی ملک میں تصرف کرنے والا نہ متعدی ہوتا ہے اور نہ ہی اس پر ضمان واجب ہوتا۔ اگر چہ اس کے تصرف کا ضرر دوسرے کی ملک تک متجاوز ہو جائے ۔ جیسے کسی نے اپنی زمین میں کھیت کاٹنے کے بعد باقی ماندہ گھاس پھونس جلایا۔ لیکن اس سے پڑوسی کی ملک میں سے بھی کچھ جھل گیا تو اس پر اس پڑوسی کے واسطے کچھ ضمان واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ یہ دونوں قیاس چونکہ متضاد ہیں۔ اسلئے صاحبین نے ان دونوں کو چھوڑ کر اس حدیث پر عمل کیا۔ جس کو ائمہ صحاح ستہ نے حضرت ابو ہریرہ سے روایت کیا ہے۔ یعنی حضور اقدس صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایسے شخص کے حق میں جو اپنا حصہ آزاد کر دے یوں ارشاد فرمایا ان كان غنيا و ان كان فقيراً سعى في حصة الآخر ۔ اگر یہ آزاد کرنے والا مالدار ہوں، تو اپنے شریک کے حصہ کا ضمان ہوگا اور اگر فقیر ہو تو شریک کے حصہ کے واسطے غلام کمائی کرے اس حدیث میں اللہ کے پاک رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے تقسیم فرمادی اور تقسیم شرکت کے منافی ہے یعنی اگر آزاد کرنے والا مالدار ہوتو یہ صرف ضامن ہوگا اور غلام پر سعایہ یعنی کمائی نہیں رکھی اور ا گرفتیہ ہو تو غلام پر صرف کمائی ہے۔ پس اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ آزاد کرنے والے کا خوشحال ہونا غلام کی کمائی کرنے سے مانع ہے۔ (عنایہ ) . اور امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شریک کے حصہ کی مالیت اس غلام کے پاس رک گئی تو شریک کو اختیار ہے کہ اس سے اپنے مال کا ضمان لے لے یعنی غلام سے کمائی کرائے اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے کسی آدمی کا کپڑا ہوا اڑالے گئی اور دوسرے کے رنگ کے کونڈے میں ڈالا ۔ چنانچہ کپڑا رنگین ہو گیا۔ یعنی کپڑے میں رنگ جزب ہو گیا تو کپڑے کے مالک پر واجب ہے کہ دوسرے کے رنگ کی قیمت ادا کرے۔ خواہ یہ صاحب ثوب خوشحال ہو یا مفلس ہو کیونکہ کپڑے والے کے پاس اس کا رنگ رک گیا ہے تو اس کو تاوان لینا جائز ہے۔ پس ایسا ہی حکم یہاں ہے۔ لیکن اتنی بات ہے کہ اگر غلام با لکل فقیر ہو تو وہ غلام سے کمائی کرا کے وصول کرلے۔ اور صاحبین کی پیش کردہ حدیث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بطور شرط کے تقسیم فرمائی ہے۔ یعنی سعایہ کو آزد کرنے والے کی مفلسی پر معلق کیا ہے اور یہ عدم فقر کے وقت استعاء یعنی کمائی کرانے کے منافی نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ جس چیز کو شرط پر معلق کیا جائے وجو د شرط وقت اس کا موجود ہونا تو ضروری ہے لیکن عدم شرط کے وقت اس کا معدوم ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ مثلا کسی نے اپنے غلام سے کہا اگر تو ھے

كتاب العناق
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم میں داخل ہوا تو ، تو آزاد ہے۔ پس گھر میں داخل ہونے کی صورت میں غلام یقیناً آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ لیکن داخل نہ ہونے کی صورت میں آزاد نہ ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ آزاد ہو سکتا ہے بایں طور کہ مولیٰ اس سے انت حر بغیر کسی شرط کے کہہ دے۔ پس اسی طرح اس مسئلہ میں بھی آزاد کرنے والے کی مالداری کے باوجود غلام سے کمائی کرائی جاسکتی ہے۔ واضح ہو کہ آزاد کرنے والا جس پر تاوان واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اسکے مالدار ہونے میں سیارہ تیسیر معتبر ہے۔ نہ کہ بیسار غناء اور بسیار تیسیر یہ ہے کہ اتنے مال کا مالک ہو کہ شریک کے حصہ کی قیمت اداء کر سکے اور یہ مقدار اس کے کپٹروں اور اس کے عیال کے خرچہ سے فاضل ہو۔ یہی ظاہر الروایۃ ہے اور اسی کے قائل امام شافعی ، امام مالک اور امام احمد ہیں اور بعض مشائخ نے حرمان نصاب کا اعتبار کیا ہے۔ لیکن پسندیدہ مسلک وہ ہے جو ظاہر الروایۃ میں ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ لیار تیسیر یعنی آسانی سے قیمت دینے کا لحاظ رکھنے میں دونوں کی رعایت کی جاتی ہے۔ کیونکہ آزاد کرنے والے نے جو چاہا لیمی ثواب اور تقرب الی اللہ آزاد کرنے کی وجہ سے وہ اس کو حاصل ہو جائے گا اور اس کے شریک ساکت کو اپنا حق پہنچ جائے گا۔
صاحبین کے قول آزاد ہونے کی وجہ
العياد
ثم التخريج على قولهما ظاهر فعدم رجوع المعتق بماضمن على لعدم السعاية في حالة اليسار و الولاء للمعتق لان العتق كله من جهته لعدم التجزى واما التخريج على قوله فخيار الاعتاق لقيام ملكه في الباقي اذا لاعتاق يتجزى عنده والتضمين لان المعتق جان عليه بافساد نصيبه حيث امتنع عليه البيع والهبة و نحو ذالك مماسوى الاعتاق وتوابعه والاستسعاء لما بينا ويرجع المتعق بما ضمن على العبد لانه قام مقام الساكت باداء الضمان وقد كان له ذالك بالاستسعاء فكذالك للمعتق ولانه ملكه باداء الضمان ضمنا فيصير كان الكل له وقد اعتق بعضه فله ان يعتق الباقى اويستسعى ان شاء والولاء للمعتق في هذا الوجه لان العتق كله من جهته حيث ملكه باداء الضمان
ترجمہ پھر صاحبین کے قول پر تخریج (حکم نکالنا ) ظاہر ہے۔ پس آزاد کرنے والے کا غلام سے مال عمان واپس نہ لینا اسلئے ہے کہ خوشحال کی حالت میں غلام پر سعایہ واجب نہیں ہے اور ولاء آزاد کرنے والے کے واسطے ہے۔ کیونکہ پوری آزادی آزاد کرنے والے کی طرف سے ہے۔ اسلئے کہ (آزادی) متجری نہیں ہوتی اور رہا امام صاحب کے قول پر تخریج کرنا، سو (شریک کو اپنا حصہ ) آزاد کرنے کا اختیار ہے۔ کیونکہ باقی میں اس کی ملک قائم ہے۔ کیونکہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک اعتناق کے ٹکڑے ہو سکتے ہیں اور تاوان لینے کا ( حق ) اسلئے ہے کہ آزاد کرنے والا (اپنے) شریک کے حصہ کو خراب کرنے کی وجہ سے اس پر ظلم کرنے والا ہے۔ چنانچہ اس پر سوائے آزاد کرنے اور اس کے توابع اور کمائی کرا لینے کے بیچنا اور ہبہ کرنا وغیرہ ممتنع ہے۔ اصل دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے اور آزاد کرنے والا تاوان کی رقم غلام سے واپس لے گا۔ کیونکہ آزاد کرنے والا تاوان دے کر ساکت کے قائم مقام ہو گیا اور ساکت کو یہ اختیار تھا کہ غلام سے کمائی کرائے ۔ پس ایسے ہی آزاد کرنے والے کو بھی یہ اختیار ہوگا اور اس وجہ سے کہ آزاد کرنے والا ادائے مہمان کی وجہ سے ضمناً اس غلام کا مالک ہو گیا۔ تو ایسا ہو جائے گا۔ گویا پورا غلام اسی کا ہے۔ حال یہ کہ اس نے اس کا ایک جز آزاد کیا ہے۔ تو اس کو اختیار ہے کہ باقی کو آزاد کر دے یا اگر چاہے تو کمائی کرا کے قیمت لے لے اور اس صورت میں ولاء آزاد کرنے والے کیلئے ہوگی۔ کیونکہ پورے غلام کی آزادی
Book of Emancipation
310
...and reward and blessing he will obtain, and the silent partner will receive his right.
Ashraf al-Bidayah Sharh Urdu Bidayah Volume 3
Explanation: The author of Hidayah said: This issue—whether the freeing person can take back from the slave after paying the amount to his partner or not—is based on two principles. The first principle: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, emancipation can be partitioned; according to the Sahibayn, emancipation cannot be partitioned, as we have explained in the first chapter. The second principle: When the freeing person is wealthy, according to Imam [Abu Hanifa] it does not prevent the slave from earning (sa'yah), while according to the Sahibayn it prevents. The proofs for the first principle have passed previously. As for the second principle, the substance of the Sahibayn's proof is that in this issue, analogy (qiyas) specifies one of two matters: either the freeing person is wealthy or poor—in both cases, the freeing person owes a guarantee (daman) to his partner, because by freeing his share he has ruined his partner's share, since it becomes impossible for him to retain his ownership and dispose of his share; and guarantee for spoilage does not differ due to wealth or poverty. The second matter is that no guarantee is required at all, because the freeing person disposed of his own share, and one who disposes of his own property is neither a transgressor nor liable for guarantee, even if his action harms another's property; like someone who burns leftover grass after harvesting his field, and some of his neighbor's property also burns—he is not liable for any guarantee to that neighbor. Since these two analogies are contradictory, the Sahibayn abandoned both and acted upon the hadith narrated by the authors of the Six Books from Abu Hurairah: The Holy Prophet (peace be upon him) said regarding a person who frees his share: 'If he is wealthy, and if he is poor, let the slave work for the other's share.' In this hadith, the Messenger of Allah made a division, and division is contrary to partnership; that is, if the freeing person is wealthy, he is only a guarantor and no earning (sa'yah) is imposed on the slave; if he is poor, there is only earning on the slave. This shows that the freeing person's being wealthy prevents the slave from earning. (al-'Inayah). And the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that the value of the partner's share remains with the slave, so the partner has the option to take his property from him through guarantee, i.e., make the slave earn; this is like a person's cloth being carried away by wind and falling into another's dye pot, where the cloth becomes dyed—the owner of the cloth must pay the value of the dye, whether the owner is wealthy or poor, because the dye remains with the cloth owner, so he can take compensation. Similarly is the ruling here. However, if the slave is completely poor, then he recovers through the slave's earnings. As for the Sahibayn's presented hadith, the response is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) made the division conditionally, i.e., he suspended sa'yah on the freeing person's poverty, and this does not contradict demanding earning in the absence of poverty, because when something is suspended on a condition, its existence at the time of the condition is necessary, but its non-existence at the time of absence of the condition is not necessary. For example, if someone says to his slave: 'If you enter the house, you are free.' Then if he enters, he is certainly free; but if he does not enter, it does not necessitate that he not be free—he may become free by the master simply saying 'You are free' without any condition. Similarly, in this issue, even if the freeing person is wealthy, earning can be required from the slave.
Be clear: For the freeing person on whom compensation (damān) is obligatory, ease of paying (yasar al-taysīr) is considered, not abundance of wealth. Yasar al-taysīr means he possesses enough wealth to pay the value of the partner's share, over and above his debts and his family's expenses. This is the position of Zahir al-Riwayah, and it is also held by Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad. Some mashā'ikh considered the nisāb of zakat as the criterion, but the preferred view is that of Zahir al-Riwayah. The reason is that by considering ease of payment, consideration is given to both parties—the freeing person obtains the reward and nearness to Allah due to freeing, and his silent partner receives his right.
The reason for the Sahibayn's statement about emancipation...
Then the takhrīj (derivation) according to their statement is apparent: the freeing person does not reclaim the amount he paid because there is no sa'yah in the case of wealth, and the walā' (clientage) belongs to the freeing person because the entire emancipation is from him, due to the non-partition of emancipation. As for takhrīj according to his (Abu Hanifa's) statement: The partner has the choice of freeing because his ownership remains in the remaining share, since emancipation is partitioned according to him; and the guarantee is because the freeing person has wronged him by spoiling his share, so sale, gift, etc. are prevented for him except emancipation and its consequences, and istis'ā' as we have explained. And the freeing person reclaims what he guaranteed from the slave, because he stood in the place of the silent partner by paying the guarantee, and the silent partner had that right through istis'ā', so likewise for the freeing person; also because by paying the guarantee he implicitly owned the slave, so it is as if the whole slave is his, and he has freed a part of him, so he may either free the rest or demand istis'ā' if he wishes. And walā' in this case belongs to the freeing person, because the entire emancipation is from him, since he owned the slave by paying the guarantee.
Translation: Then takhrīj according to the Sahibayn's statement is apparent. So the freeing person's not reclaiming the amount from the slave is because sa'yah is not obligatory in the state of wealth, and walā' is for the freeing person because the entire freedom is from him, since emancipation is not partitioned. As for takhrīj according to Imam (Abu Hanifa)'s statement, the partner has the option to free his share because his ownership remains in the remaining share, since according to Imam emancipation can be partitioned. And the right to claim compensation is because the freeing person is oppressor by spoiling his partner's share. Thus, for him, except for freeing and its consequences and demanding earning, selling, gifting, etc. are prevented due to the original proof we have mentioned. And the freeing person will take back the amount of compensation from the slave, because by paying compensation he stood in the place of the silent partner, and the silent partner had this option to demand earning from the slave, so likewise the freeing person will have this option; also because by paying compensation he implicitly became the owner of the slave, so it becomes as if the whole slave is his, yet he has freed a part of him, so he has the option to free the rest or if he wishes to demand earning and take the value. And in this case, walā' belongs to the freeing person because the entire emancipation is from him, since he owned the slave by paying compensation.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah (Ashraf al-Hidayah) addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a co-owner who frees his share of a jointly-owned slave. The central question: after the freeing co-owner pays the other co-owner (the silent partner) the value of his share, can the freeing co-owner reclaim that amount from the slave? The author explains that this issue hinges on two foundational principles: (1) whether emancipation can be partitioned (tajazzi' al-'itq)—Abu Hanifa holds it can, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold it cannot; (2) whether the freeing co-owner's wealth prevents requiring the slave to work (sa'yah) to pay off the co-owner's share—Abu Hanifa says it does not prevent, the Sahibayn say it does. The Sahibayn rely on a hadith from Abu Hurairah where the Prophet (peace be upon him) distinguished between a wealthy and a poor freeing co-owner: if wealthy, he must guarantee the other's share (without sa'yah); if poor, the slave must work (sa'yah). Abu Hanifa responds that the hadith's conditionality does not negate the possibility of requiring sa'yah from the slave even when the freeing co-owner is wealthy, just as a conditional emancipation (e.g., 'if you enter the house you are free') does not preclude unconditional emancipation. Abu Hanifa analogizes to a case where someone's cloth falls into another's dye—the owner must pay for the dye regardless of his wealth, because the dye remains with him. Similarly, the value of the silent partner's share remains with the slave, so the slave can be made to work. The passage then discusses the criterion for 'wealth' (yasar al-taysīr)—Zahir al-Riwayah holds it is having enough to pay the share over debts and family expenses, not simply possessing nisāb. Finally, the passage provides takhrīj (derivation of rulings) according to both positions: according to the Sahibayn, the freeing co-owner cannot reclaim from the slave because no sa'yah in wealth, and walā' belongs to him; according to Abu Hanifa, the freeing co-owner may reclaim from the slave, may free the remaining share, or may demand sa'yah, and walā' belongs to him because he owns the entire slave implicitly by paying the guarantee.

Key Terms
اعتاق (i'tāq): Emancipation of a slave; freeing a slave from bondage.
سعاية (sa'āyah): The act of the slave working to earn money to pay off his master's debt or to compensate a co-owner for the freed share.
ضمان (ḍamān): Guarantee; financial liability to compensate for loss or damage. Here, the freeing master's liability to pay the co-owner the value of his share.
يسار تيسير (yasār al-taysīr): Financial ease; the condition of having sufficient wealth beyond debts and family expenses to pay the co-owner's share without hardship.
ولاء (walā'): Clientage; the bond of loyalty and inheritance between the emancipator and the freed slave. The walā' belongs to the one who effectuates the full emancipation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding a co-owner freeing his share of a jointly-owned slave, what is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position regarding the slave's obligation to work (sa'yah) when the freeing co-owner is wealthy?
A) The slave must work to pay the co-owner's share regardless of the freeing master's wealth.
B) The slave must work only if the freeing master is poor; if the freeing master is wealthy, he pays the co-owner and the slave is free without obligation.
C) The slave is freed immediately and no payment is required from anyone.
D) The slave must work only if the freeing master is wealthy.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school is that a wealthy co-owner who frees his share must pay the other co-owner and cannot reclaim from the slave; only a poor co-owner can require the slave to work.

Ruling on Insolvent Co-Owner Freeing Share: Hanafi & Shafi'i Dispute
Explains Hanafi ruling and Shafi'i difference when manumitter is insolvent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when an insolvent co-owner frees his share of a slave, explain the Shafi'i objection, and apply the Hanafi rebuttal based on the principle of istis'a'.

Core Idea
When the manumitter is insolvent, the silent partner may free his share or seek earnings, but the slave cannot recover from the manumitter.

This lesson examines an inter-madhhab dispute from al-Hidayah concerning a jointly-owned slave when one co-owner (the manumitter) is insolvent and frees his share. The Hanafi school provides the silent partner with two options, while Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the silent partner's share remains untouched. We will unpack the reasoning behind each position and see how the Hanafi school uses qiyas and the concept of detention of wealth to rebut the Shafi'i argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling for the silent partner
Read the opening lines to find the two permissible options: freeing his own share or having the slave earn the value of his share. Note that wala' goes to the manumitter in both cases.
The silent partner is not obligated to do anything; he has a choice.
2
Understand why the slave cannot recover from the insolvent manumitter
The text explains that the slave earns for his own liberation, not to pay a debt. Since nothing is due from the insolvent, he cannot recover.
This is a consensus among Abu Hanifa and the two companions.
3
Compare with the mortgaged slave case
Analyze the analogy: in the mortgaged slave case, the slave earns for a debt of the pawner or for his already freed neck, so he can recover. This highlights the distinction.
The qiyas shows that the far' (joint-ownership case) has a different illa.
4
State the Shafi'i position for the insolvent manumitter
According to al-Shafi'i, the silent partner's share remains in his ownership; it can be sold or gifted. He bases this on the lack of a way to hold the partner liable (tadhmin), the slave not being an aggressor, and the harm of freeing the entire slave.
For a wealthy manumitter, al-Shafi'i agrees with the Hanafi position.
5
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi school responds that istis'a' is valid because it relies on detention of wealth, not the slave's aggression. One cannot combine ownership strength and weakness in the same person.
This rebuttal uses a rational argument (dalil aqli) rather than textual proof.

کیئے جانے پر راضی ہوا۔ کیونکہ رضا مندی بغیر علم کے مستحق نہیں ہوتی اور یہاں مولیٰ نے بغیر غلام کے علم کے اس کو آزاد کیا ہے۔ لہذا غلام کی
And in the case of the manumitter's insolvency: if he wishes, he may free (his share) due to the continuation of his ownership; and if he wishes, he may seek earnings (istis'a') from the slave for what we have stated. The right of clientage (wala') belongs to him in both cases, because the emancipation is from him. And the one from whom earnings are sought (the slave) cannot recover from the manumitter what he paid, by consensus among us, because the slave earns for the liberation of his own neck, and does not pay a debt that is upon the manumitter, since nothing is due from him due to his insolvency. Unlike the mortgaged slave, when an insolvent pawner frees him, because the slave earns for his own neck which has been freed, or he pays a debt that is upon the pawner; for this reason he recovers from him. And Imam al-Shafi'i's view regarding the wealthy (manumitter) is like that of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). But regarding the insolvent, he said: the silent partner's share remains in his ownership; it may be sold or gifted. Because there is no way to hold the partner liable due to his insolvency, nor to seek earnings from the slave, since the slave is neither an aggressor nor consenting to emancipation, nor to free the entire slave because of harm to the silent partner. So what we have determined is determined. We reply: there is a way to seek earnings because it does not require aggression; rather it is based on the detention of wealth (the value of the share). So one cannot combine in one person both the strength that necessitates ownership and the weakness that negates it. Translation: And in the case of the manumitter's insolvency, if he wishes, he may free his share; if he wishes, he may seek earnings from the slave for the reason we have stated. In both cases, the silent partner's clientage (wala') goes to him, because the emancipation is from him. And the slave from whom earnings have been sought cannot take back the paid amount from his manumitter. Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions are agreed on this. This is because the slave earns for the liberation of his own neck, and does not pay a debt that is upon the manumitter, since nothing is due from the manumitter due to his insolvency. Unlike the mortgaged slave, when an insolvent pawner frees him, because the slave earns for his own neck while his neck has already been freed, or he pays a debt that was upon the pawner, so he recovers from the pawner. And Imam al-Shafi'i's view regarding the wealthy is like the two companions; but regarding the insolvent, he said: the silent partner's share remains in his ownership; it can be sold or gifted. Because there is no way to make the partner liable due to insolvency, nor to seek earnings from the slave because the slave is not an aggressor nor consenting to emancipation, nor to free the entire slave due to harm to the silent partner. So what we have determined is determined. And we reply: there is a way to seek earnings because it does not need aggression; rather it is based on the detention of the wealth (the value of the share). So these two things—strength which is the cause of ownership and weakness which negates strength—cannot be combined in one person. Explanation: All the previous details were when the manumitter was wealthy. If the manumitter is insolvent, the silent partner has the option: if he wishes, he may free his share because his ownership remains; and if he wishes, he may seek earnings from the slave because the value of his share is detained with the slave. In the case where the silent partner seeks earnings from the slave, the slave cannot take this money back from his manumitter. Abu Hanifa and the two companions are agreed on this ruling. This is because the slave earns to free his own neck, and does not pay a debt that is upon the manumitter, since nothing is due from the manumitter due to his insolvency. Unlike the mortgaged slave when the pawner frees him while insolvent, because the slave earns his price and gives it to the pledgee and then recovers from the pawner. The proof is that the slave has earned for his own price while his neck had been freed, or he has paid a debt that was upon the pawner, so he recovers from the pawner. The author of al-Hidayah says: if the manumitter is wealthy, then Imam al-Shafi'i's view is like the two companions. But if the manumitter is insolvent, then Imam al-Shafi'i's school is that the silent partner's share remains in his ownership, whether he sells his share or gives it as a gift. That is, his full ownership remains in his share. Because the silent partner can neither make the manumitter liable for his share since the manumitter is insolvent, nor has he the option to seek earnings from the slave because the slave has not committed aggression nor has he consented to being freed. Since consent is not valid without knowledge, and here the master has freed him without the slave's knowledge, therefore the slave... (text cuts off).
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage from al-Hidayah deals with an inter-madhhab dispute regarding a jointly-owned slave when one co-owner frees his share but is insolvent (mu'sir). The passage begins with the Hanafi ruling, explains the reasoning, contrasts with the analogous case of a mortgaged slave, and then presents Imam al-Shafi'i's view followed by the Hanafi rebuttal. The Hanafi position (agreeing both Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn) gives the silent partner (sharik sakin) two options: (1) free his own share, or (2) have the slave earn (istis'a') the value of his share. In both cases, the right of clientage (wala') goes to the manumitter because the emancipation originates from him. The slave cannot recover the earned amount from the insolvent manumitter because the slave earns to free himself, not to satisfy a debt of the manumitter. This is unlike the case of a mortgaged slave freed by an insolvent pawner, where the slave can recover because his earnings go to pay off the pawner's debt or to redeem his already freed neck. Al-Shafi'i, on the other hand, holds that when the manumitter is insolvent, the silent partner's share remains untouched in his ownership; he may sell or gift it because there is no way to compel the silent partner to accept liability (tadhmin) from the insolvent manumitter, nor to force the slave to earn (istis'a') since the slave did not commit aggression and did not consent to freedom, and freeing the entire slave would harm the silent partner. The Hanafi response is that istis'a' is permissible here because it does not rely on the slave's wrongdoing; rather it is based on the principle that the value of the silent partner's share is detained (ihtibas) with the slave. Therefore, one cannot combine in one person both the strength (ownership) and weakness (inability to earn) that would negate that strength. The text then clarifies that the earlier details were for the wealthy manumitter, and now the ruling for the insolvent is given. Finally, the author of al-Hidayah summarizes al-Shafi'i's position: for the wealthy, al-Shafi'i agrees with the Sahibayn; for the insolvent, he leaves the silent partner's share in his full ownership with no recourse.

Key Terms
معتق (mu'tiq): The person who emancipates a slave, i.e., the manumitter.
معسر (mu'sir): A person who is insolvent, lacking the financial means to pay a debt or compensation.
ولاء (wala'): The right of clientage that belongs to the manumitter over the freed slave, which gives the manumitter inheritance rights from the slave under certain conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, when one co-owner of a slave frees his share while insolvent, what options does the silent partner have?
A) He can only free his own share.
B) He can either free his own share or have the slave earn the value of his share.
C) He must free the entire slave.
D) He can only seek compensation from the manumitter.

Key Takeaway
When the manumitter is insolvent, the silent partner may free his share or seek earnings; the slave does not recover from the manumitter.
