The Stranger's Option: Su'aya with a Wealthy Manumitter
Ruling when stranger buys half then father buys other half

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position and the Sahibayn's position on the stranger's option when a wealthy father buys the remaining half of a jointly-owned slave, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A stranger who buys half first retains an option despite lack of consent; Abu Hanifa allows su'aya even if the manumitter is wealthy.

This lesson examines a specific scenario within the broader Hanafi discourse on joint ownership of a slave who is the father's son. The stranger purchases half first, then the father independently buys the other half while he is wealthy. The key question: does the stranger have a right to make the slave work (su'aya) for his share, or must he claim compensation from the father? You will trace the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and understand the practical consequence of their disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Note the sequence: stranger buys half first, then the father buys the other half. The father is wealthy. The stranger did not consent to the loss of his share.
This differs from the case where the father buys first.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position
Abu Hanifa holds that the stranger has a choice (khayar): he may either hold the father responsible for compensation (daman) or make the slave work (su'aya) for half his value. The wealth of the manumitter does not prevent su'aya.
The slave's value is considered held back (ihtibas) with him.
3
State Sahibayn's Position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) hold that the stranger has no choice; the father must pay compensation directly. The slave cannot be forced to work because the manumitter's wealth prevents su'aya.
For Sahibayn, su'aya is only allowed when the manumitter is poor.
4
Analyze the Reasoning (Ta'lil)
The difference revolves around whether 'yusr al-mu'tiq' (wealth of the manumitter) is a valid preventer (mani') of su'aya. Abu Hanifa sees no such restriction; Sahibayn treat wealth as a bar.
Both sides agree the stranger did not consent, but disagree on the consequence.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
If the stranger chooses su'aya under Abu Hanifa, the slave works to pay half his value. Under Sahibayn, the father must pay this amount immediately. The practical outcome differs in who bears the burden.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is typically Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اجنبی نے نصف خرید ا پھر باپ نے دوسرے نصف کو خریدا حالانکہ باپ خوشحال ہے اجنبی کو خیار ہے اگر چاہے باپ کو ضامن ٹھہرائے
و ان بدأ الاجنبى فاشترى نصفه ثم اشترى الاب نصفه الآخر و هو موسرفا لاجنبى بالخياران شاء ضمن الاب لانه مارضى بافساد نصيبه و ان شاء استسعى الا بن فى نصف قيمته لاحتباس ماليته عنده و هذا عند ابي حنيفة لان يسار المعتق لا يمنع السعاية عنده وقالا لا خيار له و يضمن الاب نصف قيمته لا يسار المعتق يمنع السعاية عندهما
ترجمہ اور اگر پہلے اجنبی نے اس غلام کے نصف کو خریدا۔ پھر باپ نے اس کے نصف آخر کو خریدا۔ حالانکہ اسکا باپ مالدار ہے۔ تو اجنبی کو اختیار ہے چاہے باپ سے ناوان لے۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنا حصہ خراب ہونے پر راضی نہیں ہوا اور چاہے بیٹے سے اس کی نصف قیمت کے واسطے کمائی کرائے۔ کیونکہ بیٹے کے پاس اس کی مالیت رکی ہوئی ہے اور یہ ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے۔ اسلئے کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک آزاد کرنے والے کی خوشحالی سے غلام کا سعی کرنا متنع نہیں ہوتا اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ سعی کرانے کا اختیار نہیں ہے بلکہ باپ اسکی نصف قیمت کا تاوان دے گا۔ اسلئے کہ صاحبین کے نزدیک آزاد کرنے والے کا خوشحال ہونا مانع سعایہ ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ پہلے ایک اجنبی نے غلام کا نصف خریدا۔ پھر اس کے باپ نے اس کے نصف آخر خرید لیا۔ درانحالیکہ کے نصف آخرخریدلیا۔ غلام کا یہ باپ خوشحال ہے۔ تو اس صورت میں اجنبی شخص کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ وہ غلام کے باپ سے اپنے نصف حصہ کا تاوان لے لے۔ کیونکہ یہ اجنبی اپنا حصہ بگاڑنے پر کسی طرح راضی نہیں ہوا اور چاہے بیٹے (غلام) سے اس کی نصف قیمت کمائی کرا کے وصول کر لے۔ کیونکہ اس غلام کے پاس اس کی مالیت رکی ہوئی ہے یہ مذہب امام اعظم کا ہے۔ اسلئے کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک آزاد کرنے والے کا مالدار ہونا مانع سعایہ نہیں ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اجنبی کو غلام سے کمائی کرانے کا اختیار نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کی نصف قیمت کا باپ کو ضامن بنائے گا۔ کیونکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک بسیار معتق مانع سعایہ ہے۔
And if the stranger began by buying half, then the father bought the other half while he (the father) is wealthy, the stranger has a choice: if he wishes, he can hold the father responsible (damin), because he did not consent to the corruption of his share; and if he wishes, he can make the son (the slave) work (say'a) for half his price, because his wealth is held back with him. And this is according to Abu Hanifa, because according to him the wealth of the manumitter does not prevent su'aya. And they (the Sahibayn) said: he has no choice; the father is responsible for half the price, because according to them the wealth of the manumitter prevents su'aya. Translation: And if the stranger bought half of the slave first, then the father bought the remaining half, while the father is wealthy, then the stranger has a choice: if he wishes, he takes compensation from the father, because he did not agree to the destruction of his share; and if he wishes, he makes the son (the slave) work to pay half the price, because the slave's value is held back with him. This is according to Abu Hanifa, because according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the wealth of the manumitter does not prevent the slave from working (su'aya). And the Sahibayn said: he has no such choice; rather, the father will pay compensation for half the price, because according to them, the wealth of the manumitter prevents su'aya. Commentary: The scenario is that a stranger bought half of the slave, then the father bought the other half while wealthy. In this case, the stranger has the option to claim compensation from the father, because he did not consent to the loss of his share, or to make the son (slave) work to recover half the price, because the slave's value is tied up with him. This is the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa. According to him, the wealth of the manumitter does not prevent su'aya. According to the Sahibayn, the stranger does not have the right to make the slave work; rather, he must make the father responsible for half the price, because in their view the wealth of the manumitter prevents su'aya.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage presents a specific scenario within the broader dispute on joint ownership of a slave who is the father's son. Here, the stranger buys his half first, then the father buys the other half. The key difference from the previous case is that the stranger did not enter into partnership with the father; rather, he first owned half, and then the father independently purchased the other half. Consequently, the stranger did not consent to the destruction of his share. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the stranger still has a choice: he can either demand compensation from the wealthy father (since the father's purchase effected automatic emancipation of his share, harming the stranger's half) or he can make the slave work (istis'a') to earn the value of the stranger's half. This is because Abu Hanifa holds that even a wealthy manumitter does not prevent the slave from working for the partner. The Sahibayn disagree: the stranger has no choice; he must demand compensation from the father, because if the manumitter is wealthy, the slave cannot be required to work. The stranger did not consent, so the father is liable. The commentary explains the scenario and difference.

Key Terms
خیار (khayar): A choice or option given to the stranger between taking compensation from the father or making the slave work.
سعایہ (su'aya): The slave working to earn money to compensate the stranger for his share.
یسر معتق (yusr mu'tiq): The wealth or affluence of the manumitter (the father).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when a stranger buys half of a slave first, and then the father (who is wealthy) buys the other half, what options does the stranger have?
A) He can only make the father pay compensation.
B) He can only make the slave work.
C) He can either make the father pay compensation or make the slave work.
D) He must free his own share.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa grants the stranger a choice between compensation from the father or su'aya from the slave, even if the manumitter is wealthy; Sahibayn restrict this.

Father Buys Half His Son: Daman Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on father's purchase of half-son

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on daman when a father buys half his son from the full owner and distinguish between Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa says no guarantee; Sahibayn say guarantee if father is wealthy.

When a father purchases half of his own son from the full owner, the purchase automatically frees that half because a father cannot own his child. The question then arises: must the father compensate the seller for the lost value? This passage presents the intra-Hanafi disagreement on this point.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its immediate effect
Recognize that a father buying his son (even half) results in immediate emancipation of that share. This is the foundational fact underlying the dispute.
The emancipation occurs by operation of law, not by the father's intention.
2
Understand the issue of daman
The seller loses the value of the half that was freed. The dispute is whether the father must pay the seller the value of that half as daman (guarantee).
Daman here means liability to pay compensation.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position and his reasoning
Abu Hanifa holds that no daman is required, even if the father is wealthy. His reasoning: the seller entered into the sale knowing the father is a close relative, thus implicitly consented to the emancipation and its consequences.
The seller's consent is inferred from the nature of the transaction.
4
State the Sahibayn's position and their reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) hold that if the father is wealthy, he must pay daman to the seller. Their reasoning: the seller did not explicitly consent to losing the value; the father's wealth makes him able to compensate, so justice requires payment.
The Sahibayn consider the seller's loss and the father's ability to pay.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical difference is whether the father pays anything. If he is wealthy, Abu Hanifa says no payment, Sahibayn say half the price. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hidayah is typically Abu Hanifa's view.
The text says 'the reason we have already mentioned', indicating the author's preference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جس شخص نے اپنے بیٹے کا نصف خریدا اور وہ خوشحال ہے اس پر ضمان ہے یا نہیں ، اقوال فقہاء
ومن اشترى نصف ابنه وهو مو سر فلاضمان عليه عند ابي حنيفة وقالا يضمن اذا كان موسر او معناه اذا اشتری نصفه ممن یملک کله فلايضمن لبائعه شيئا عنده والوجه قد ذكرناه

And concerning the person who bought half of his son while he is wealthy: there is no guarantee upon him according to Abu Hanifa, and they (Sahibayn) said: he is responsible if he is wealthy. The meaning of this issue: if he bought half from the one who owns the whole (the full owner), then he is not responsible for anything to the seller according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and the reason we have already mentioned.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage presents a brief ruling on a distinct scenario: a father buys half of his own son (who is a slave) from the full owner. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the father is not liable for any guarantee (daman) to the seller, even if the father is wealthy. The Sahibayn hold that if the father is wealthy, he is liable. The reason is the same as discussed earlier: the father's purchase of his son effects immediate emancipation of that half (since buying a close relative frees), which invalidates the seller's remaining interest? Actually, here the seller is the full owner selling half; the father's purchase frees that half, so the seller loses half the slave's value. Abu Hanifa argues that the seller consented to the sale knowing the father is a close relative, so no guarantee. The Sahibayn say the seller did not consent to the loss, so the father must compensate if wealthy. The text notes the reason has been previously stated.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee to pay the seller the value of the portion that became free.

In the Hanafi school, when a father buys half his son from the full owner, Abu Hanifa rules no daman due to implied consent, while the Sahibayn require daman if the father is wealthy; the relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's.

The Stranger's Option When a Father Buys His Son's Other Half
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the stranger's option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the stranger's option (khiyar) when a father buys his son's other half, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa gives the stranger an option; the Sahibayn don't—the father's wealth blocks the slave's earning.

This passage presents a specific transactional scenario involving a slave, a stranger, and the slave's father. The Hanafi school is divided on the remedy available to the stranger. Understanding this dispute reveals the usul principle of 'yasar al-mu'tiq' and how it affects the applicability of seeking earnings (saya).

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
Trace the facts: A stranger buys half a slave. Then the slave's father buys the other half. The father is wealthy (muyasir).
Note that the father is explicitly described as 'musir' (wealthy).
2
State the Hanafi position
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the stranger has an option (khiyar): he can either hold the father liable (daman) for half the slave's value or make the slave seek earnings (saya) for half his value.
The basis is that the father's wealth does not prevent saya according to Abu Hanifa.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the stranger has no option; he must hold the father liable immediately. Making the slave seek earnings is not permitted because the father's wealth prevents saya.
This is a clear intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the effect of yasar al-mu'tiq.
4
Analyze the underlying usul principle
The difference hinges on the weight given to yasar al-mu'tiq (wealth of the manumitter). For the Sahibayn, wealth of the manumitter is a bar to saya; for Abu Hanifa, it is not.
This is a usul al-fiqh difference: the scope of the principle that prevents saya.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifa, the stranger may choose to have the slave work, which may take time. Under the Sahibayn, the father must pay immediately.
The mufta bihi is not given in this passage; later tarjih may favor one view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اجنبی نے نصف خریدا پھر باپ نے دوسرے نصف کو خریدا حالانکہ باپ خوشحال ہے اجنبی کو خیار ہے اگر چاہے باپ کو ضامن ٹھہرائے
و ان بدأ الاجنبى فاشترى نصفه ثم اشترى الاب نصفه الآخر و هو موسر فللاجنبى بالخيار ان شاء ضمن الاب لانه ما رضى بافساد نصيبه و ان شاء استسعى الابن فى نصف قيمته لاحتباس ماليته عنده و هذا عند ابي حنيفة لان يسار المعتق لا يمنع السعاية عنده وقالا لا خيار له و يضمن الاب نصف قيمته لان يسار المعتق يمنع السعاية عندهما
ترجمہ اور اگر پہلے اجنبی نے اس غلام کے نصف کو خریدا۔ پھر باپ نے اس کے نصف آخر کو خریدا۔ حالانکہ اس کا باپ مالدار ہے۔ تو اجنبی کو اختیار ہے چاہے باپ سے ضمان لے۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنا حصہ خراب ہونے پر راضی نہیں ہوا اور چاہے بیٹے سے اس کی نصف قیمت کے واسطے کمائی کرائے۔ کیونکہ بیٹے کے پاس اس کی مالیت رکی ہوئی ہے اور یہ ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے۔ اس لئے کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک آزاد کرنے والے کی خوشحالی سے غلام کا سعی کرنا ممنوع نہیں ہوتا اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ سعی کرانے کا اختیار نہیں ہے بلکہ باپ اس کی نصف قیمت کا تاوان دے گا۔ اس لئے کہ صاحبین کے نزدیک آزاد کرنے والے کا خوشحال ہونا مانع سعایہ ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ پہلے ایک اجنبی نے غلام کا نصف خریدا۔ پھر اس کے باپ نے اس کے نصف آخر خرید لیا۔ درانحالیکہ وہ باپ خوشحال ہے۔ تو اس صورت میں اجنبی شخص کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ وہ غلام کے باپ سے اپنے نصف حصہ کا تاوان لے لے۔ کیونکہ یہ اجنبی اپنا حصہ بگاڑنے پر کسی طرح راضی نہیں ہوا اور چاہے بیٹے (غلام) سے اس کی نصف قیمت کمائی کرا کے وصول کر لے۔ کیونکہ اس غلام کے پاس اس کی مالیت رکی ہوئی ہے یہ مذہب امام اعظم کا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک آزاد کرنے والے کا مالدار ہونا مانع سعایہ نہیں ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اجنبی کو غلام سے کمائی کرانے کا اختیار نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کی نصف قیمت کا باپ کو ضامن بنائے گا۔ کیونکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک يسار المعتق مانع سعایہ ہے۔
A stranger bought half, then the father bought the other half while the father is wealthy. The stranger has the option: if he wishes, he holds the father liable for the value of his half, because he did not consent to the corruption of his share; and if he wishes, he makes the son seek earnings for half his value, because his property is retained by the son. This is according to Abu Hanifa because the wealth of the manumitter does not prevent seeking earnings according to him. The two (Sahibayn) said: He has no option, and the father guarantees half its value, because the wealth of the manumitter prevents seeking earnings according to them. Translation: And if first the stranger bought half of this slave, then the father bought the remaining half, while his father is wealthy, then the stranger has the option: if he wishes, he takes guarantee from the father, because he did not consent to his share being spoiled; and if he wishes, he makes the son earn for half his value, because the son's property is retained. This is according to Abu Hanifa, because according to Imam the wealth of the manumitter does not prevent the slave's seeking earnings. The Sahibayn said: He does not have the option to make him seek earnings; rather, the father will pay compensation for half its value, because according to them the wealth of the manumitter prevents seeking earnings. Explanation: The situation is that first a stranger bought half of a slave, then his father bought the remaining half, while the father is wealthy. In this case, the stranger has the option to take compensation from the father for his half-share, because he did not consent to his share being spoiled, or he may make the son (the slave) earn half his value and collect it, because the slave's property is retained. This is the school of Imam Abu Hanifa because according to him the wealth of the manumitter does not prevent seeking earnings. According to the Sahibayn, the stranger does not have the option to make the slave earn; rather, he will make the father liable for half its value, because according to them the wealth of the manumitter prevents seeking earnings.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a case where a stranger first buys half of a slave, and then the slave's father purchases the other half while the father is wealthy. The issue is whether the stranger can claim the value of his half from the father or can require the slave to earn and pay half his value. Imam Abu Hanifa gives the stranger the option: he can either hold the father liable or make the slave seek earnings. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) restrict the stranger to only holding the father liable, because they consider the father's wealth a bar to seeking earnings from the slave. The commentary explains the reasoning: since the father is wealthy, he can pay the value, so the slave should not be burdened. This example illustrates the rule that the wealth of the manumitter (yasar al-mu'tiq) influences the applicability of seeking earnings (saya).

Key Terms
خیار (khiyar): An option or choice given to the stranger to either claim guarantee from the father or make the slave seek earnings.
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee; the father is held liable to pay the value of the stranger's half.
سعایة (saya/sa'aya): Seeking earnings by a partially emancipated slave to pay his value to the owner.
یسار المعتق (yasar al-mu'tiq): The wealth and financial ease of the person who manumits; it affects whether the slave can be made to seek earnings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for the Sahibayn's denial of the stranger's option to make the slave seek earnings?
A) The stranger did not consent to his share being spoiled.
B) The father's wealth prevents seeking earnings.
C) The slave's property is retained by him.
D) The father is not liable for the value.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a father buys his son's other half from a stranger, Abu Hanifa grants the stranger an option between holding the father liable or making the slave earn; the Sahibayn restrict to holding the father liable because the father's wealth bars seeking earnings.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Liability of a Father Who Buys Half His Slave-Son
Intra-Hanafi dispute on father's liability for half of his slave-son.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the liability of a father who buys half of his slave-son, and explain the practical consequence of the dispute.

Core Idea
When a father buys half his slave-son, Abu Hanifa holds no liability; the Sahibayn hold liability if the father is wealthy.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a father who purchases half of his biological son who is enslaved and owned by a third party. The question is whether the father must pay the seller for that half. The two positions reflect differing applications of principles related to manumission and financial responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Parties and Transaction
A father buys half of his son (who is a slave) from the original owner who owns the entire son. The father is the buyer, the original owner is the seller, and the son is the slave.
The 'son' here means a biological son who is a slave in the possession of another.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the father is not liable (no daman) to pay anything to the seller, regardless of the father's wealth.
The text refers to an earlier reasoning (al-wajh) which likely involves the father's right of custody or the slave's inability to earn due to the father's status.
3
State the Sahibayn's Position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) hold that the father is liable for half the value of the son if the father is wealthy (musir).
Wealth is the key condition for their ruling.
4
Determine the Practical Difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: Under Abu Hanifa, the seller receives nothing; under the Sahibayn, the seller receives half the value from a wealthy father.
This difference directly affects the seller's right to compensation.

Source Text

ومن اشترى نصف ابنه وهو موسر فلاضمان عليه عند ابي حنيفة وقالا يضمن اذا كان موسر او معناه اذا اشتری نصفه ممن یملک کله فلايضمن لبائعه شيئا عنده والوجه قد ذكرناه

The person who bought half of his son while he is wealthy – is there liability or not? Statements of the jurists. And whoever buys half of his son while he is wealthy, there is no liability upon him according to Abu Hanifa. They (the two) said: He is liable if he is wealthy. Commentary
This passage presents another intra-Hanafi dispute. The case: A father buys half of his son (who is a slave) from the original owner who owns the entire son. The dispute hinges on the same principle: does the father's wealth prevent the slave from having to earn? Abu Hanifa's Ruling on Compensation in Co-Owned Manumission
First part of the dispute: Abu Hanifa's view with example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the options available to the silent partner and the mudabbir under Abu Hanifa's ruling and calculate the compensation amounts using the two-thirds valuation of a mudabbar.

Core Idea
The silent partner can claim 1/3 of a pure slave's value from the mudabbir; the mudabbir can claim 1/3 of the mudabbar's value from the freed partner.

This lesson examines Imam Abu Hanifa's approach to a complex case of partial manumission in a co-ownership. When three partners own a slave, and one makes him a mudabbar while another frees him outright, Abu Hanifa provides each partner with specific legal options. The silent partner may seek compensation from the mudabbir, and the mudabbir may seek compensation from the one who freed, but the amounts differ due to the reduced valuation of a mudabbar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their actions
Three partners (A, B, C) own a slave. A makes tadbir, B frees, C remains silent. All are wealthy (maysar).
Wealth is a condition for the options.
2
Understand the valuation of a mudabbar
A mudabbar is valued at two-thirds of a pure slave (qinn). This reduced value reflects the future freedom right inherent in tadbir.
This is key to calculating compensation.
3
State Abu Hanifa's options for the silent partner (C)
C can hold A liable for one-third of the value of a pure slave (i.e., C's original share), but cannot hold B liable.
C cannot claim from both; he must choose.
4
State the options for the mudabbir (A)
A can hold B liable for one-third of the value as a mudabbar (i.e., one-third of two-thirds of pure slave value), but cannot reclaim from B the one-third he paid to C.
A's claim is based on the mudabbar's value, not the pure slave's.
5
Apply the numerical example
If pure slave value = 27 dinars, mudabbar value = 18 dinars. Then C can claim 9 dinars from A. A can claim 6 dinars from B, but not the 9 dinars he paid C.
The example illustrates the fractional amounts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک غلام تین آدمیوں میں مشترک تھا ایک نے مدبر بنایا اور وہ خوشحال تھا پھر دوسرے نے آزاد کیا وہ بھی خوشحال ہے پھر تاوان چاہا ساکت کیلئے اختیار ہے کہ مدبر کرنے والے کو رقیق کی تہائی قیمت کا ضامن ٹھہرائے اور آزاد کرنے والے کو ضامن نہ بنائے
و اذا كان العبدبين ثلثة نفر فدبر احدهم وهو موسرتم اعتقه الأخرو هو موسر فارادوا الضمان فللساكت أن يضمن المدبر ثلث قيمته قناو لا يضمن المعتق وللمدبران يضمن المعتق ثلث قيمته مدبر اولا يضمنه الثلث الذى ضمن وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وقالا العبد كله للذي دبره اول مرة ويضمن ثلثي قيمته الشريكيه موسرا كان او معسرا
ترجمہ اور اگر ایک غلام تین آدمیوں کے درمیان (مشترک) ہو۔ پس ان میں سے ایک نے اسکومد بر کر دیا۔ حالانکہ یہ شخص خوشحال ہے۔ پھر دوسرے نے اس کو آزاد کر دیا اور یہ بھی خوشحال ہے۔ پھر انہوں نے تاوان چایا۔ تو خاموش رہنے والے کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ مدبر کرنے والے کو خالص رقیق کی تہائی قیمت کا ضامن بنائے اور آزاد کرنے والے کو ضامن نہ بنائے اور مدبر کرنے والے کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ آزاد کرنے والے سے اس غلام کی تہائی قیمت بحساب مدبر ہونے کے تاوان لے اور نہ ضامن بنائے اس کو اس تہائی کا جس کا وہ خود ضامن ہوا اور یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ پورا غلام اسی شخص کا ہے جس نے اس کو سب سے پہلے مدبر کر دیا تھا اور مدبر کرنے والا اس کی دو تہائی قیمت اپنے دونوں شریکوں کو تاوان دے گا خواہ وہ خوشحال ہو یا تنگدست ہو ۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ سے پہلے یہ ذہن نشین کر لیجئے کہ مدبر کی قیمت شریعت کی نظر میں رقیق ( غلام محض ) کی قیمت کا دو تہائی ہوتی ہے۔ مثلاً اگر غلام کی قیمت ۲۷ دینار ہوں تو مدبر کی قیمت ۱۸ دینار ہوں گے۔
اب صورت مسئلہ پر نظر ڈالئے صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک غلام تین شخصوں کے درمیان مشترک ہو ۔ پھر ان میں سے ایک نے اس کو مد بر کر دیا ۔ حالانکہ یہ مدبر کرنے والا شریک خوشحال ہے۔ پھر دوسرے شریک نے اس کو آزاد کر دیا اور یہ بھی خوشحال ہے۔ پھر خاموش رہنے والے اور مدبر کرنے والے شریک نے تاوان چاہا تو ساکت کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ مدبر کرنے والے شریک کو رقیق محض کی تہائی قیمت کا ضامن بنا دے اور آزاد کرنے والے کو ضامن نہیں بنائے گا اور مدبر کرنے والے کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ آزاد کرنے والے سے مدبر کی تنہائی قیمت تاوان لے لے اور جس تہائی قیمت کا وہ ساکت کے لئے ضامن ہوا تھا وہ آزاد کرنے والے سے نہیں لے سکتا ہے۔ مثلاً غلام خالص کی قیمت ۲۷ دینار ہیں تو مد بر کی قیمت اس کی دو تہائی یعنی ۱۸ دینار ہوں گے۔ پس مدبر کی قیمت کا ایک تہائی 4 دینار ہوئے اور غلام خالص کی قیمت کا ایک تہائی 9 دینار ہیں۔ پس حاصل یہ ہوا کہ مدبر کرنے والا شریک آزاد کرنے والے سے دینا ر تاوان لے سکتا ہے اور ۹ر دینار بطور تاوان نہیں لے سکتا اور یہ قول حضرت امام اعظم رحمہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا ہے اور صاحبین نے کہا کہ پورا غلام اسی شخص کا ہے جس نے اس کو سب سے پہلے مدبر کر دیا تھا اور بعد میں آزاد کرنا باطل ہے اور مدبر کرنے والا اس کی دو تہائی قیمت اپنے دو شریکوں کو دے گا۔
There was a slave shared among three persons. One made him mudabbar while he was wealthy. Then another set him free, and he too was wealthy. Then they sought compensation. The silent one has the option to hold the mudabbar liable for one-third of the value as a purely enslaved (raqiq) and not hold the one who freed liable. And the mudabbar has the option to hold the one who freed liable for one-third of the value as mudabbar, and he does not hold him liable for the one-third for which he himself became liable. This is according to Abu Hanifa. They (the two) said: The entire slave belongs to the one who first made him mudabbar, and he will compensate his two partners with two-thirds of the value, whether they are wealthy or poor. Translation: And if a slave is shared among three persons. Then one of them made him mudabbar, while this person is wealthy. Then another set him free, and he too is wealthy. Then they sought compensation. So the silent one has the option to hold the mudabbir liable for the value of one-third of a pure slave (raqiq), and not hold the one who freed liable. And the mudabbir has the option to take from the one who freed compensation for one-third of the value as mudabbar, and he does not hold him liable for the one-third for which he himself became liable. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn said: The entire slave belongs to the one who first made him mudabbar, and the mudabbir will compensate his two partners with two-thirds of its value, whether he is wealthy or poor. Explanation: Before the case, note that the value of a mudabbar in the eyes of the Sharia is two-thirds of the value of a pure slave (raqiq). For example, if the slave's value is 27 dinars, the mudabbar's value is 18 dinars. Now look at the case: If a slave is shared among three persons. Then one of them makes him mudabbar while he is wealthy. Then another partner sets him free, and he too is wealthy. Then the silent one and the mudabbir partner seek compensation. The silent one has the option to hold the mudabbir partner liable for one-third of the value of a pure slave, and he will not hold the one who freed liable. The mudabbir has the option to take from the one who freed compensation for the mudabbar's value of one-third, and he cannot take from the one who freed the one-third for which he himself became liable. For example, if the pure slave's value is 27 dinars, the mudabbar's value is two-thirds, i.e., 18 dinars. So one-third of the mudabbar's value is 6 dinars, and one-third of the pure slave's value is 9 dinars. Thus, the mudabbir partner can take 6 dinars as compensation from the one who freed, and cannot take 9 dinars as compensation. This is the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn said: The entire slave belongs to the one who first made him mudabbar, and the subsequent freeing is void. The mudabbir will give two-thirds of its value to his two partners.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage addresses a complex case of co-ownership and partial manumission. Three partners own a slave. One partner makes the slave a mudabbar (i.e., declares him free upon his death). Then another partner sets the slave free outright. Both the mudabbir and the third (silent) partner are wealthy. The dispute concerns who owes what to whom. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the silent partner has the option to claim one-third of the value of a pure slave (raqiq) from the mudabbir, or to claim from the freed partner? Actually the text says he can hold the mudabbir liable for one-third of the pure slave's value, and not hold the one who freed. Meanwhile, the mudabbir can claim from the one who freed the value of one-third of the mudabbar (which is two-thirds of the pure slave's value, so one-third of that is 2/9 of the pure slave's value). The Sahibayn hold a different view: they consider the entire slave to belong to the first mudabbir, so the subsequent freeing is ineffective. The mudabbir must compensate both partners with two-thirds of the pure slave's value, regardless of his wealth. The passage illustrates the principle that the value of a mudabbar is two-thirds of that of an absolute slave, and this affects compensation amounts.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose master has declared that he will be free upon the master's death; his value for legal purposes is two-thirds of a pure slave.
رقیق (raqiq): A slave in full ownership, not subject to any partial manumission.
ساکت (sakit): The partner who did not perform any act of manumission and remains silent.
تاوان (tawan): Compensation, indemnity paid by one partner to another for loss of share due to manumission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under Abu Hanifa's ruling, how much can the mudabbir claim from the partner who freed the slave, expressed as a fraction of the pure slave's value?
A) 1/3
B) 2/9
C) 1/9
D) 2/3

Key Takeaway
In Abu Hanifa's view, the silent partner claims 1/3 pure value from the mudabbir; the mudabbir claims 1/3 mudabbar value from the freed partner, reflecting the reduced value of a mudabbar.

intermediate
6 min
Sahibayn's Ruling: Dominance of First Tadbir
Second part of the dispute: Sahibayn's view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Sahibayn's ruling that the first tadbir gives the mudabbir full ownership of the slave and calculate the compensation he must pay to his partners.

Core Idea
The first tadbir vests full ownership in the mudabbir, voiding later manumission; he pays two-thirds of the slave's value to his partners.

This lesson presents the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) on the same scenario. They argue that the first act of tadbir creates an overriding right, so the mudabbir becomes the sole owner. Consequently, the subsequent freeing is ineffective, and the mudabbir must compensate both other partners for their shares at the full pure slave valuation.

Guided Path
1
Recall the scenario
Three partners (A, B, C) own a slave. A makes tadbir first, then B frees, C silent. All are wealthy.
Wealth is not a factor in the Sahibayn's ruling; they state 'whether wealthy or poor'.
2
State the Sahibayn's principle
The first tadbir gives the mudabbir exclusive ownership of the entire slave. The subsequent freeing is void.
This is a key difference from Abu Hanifa's proportional approach.
3
Identify the compensation obligation
The mudabbir must compensate his two partners for their shares: each originally owned one-third, so total compensation is two-thirds of the pure slave's value.
The compensation is based on the pure slave value, not the mudabbar value.
4
Note the absence of reciprocal claims
The freed partner does not pay anything, and the mudabbir cannot claim from him because his freeing act is void.
This simplifies the liability: only one party pays.
5
Contrast with Abu Hanifa
Under Abu Hanifa, the mudabbir pays less (1/3 pure value to silent) but can claim from the freed partner. Under Sahibayn, the mudabbir pays more (2/3) but has no claim.
The practical difference: total amount paid by mudabbir is different.

Under the Sahibayn's ruling, if a pure slave is valued at 60 dinars, how much does the mudabbir pay in total to his two partners?

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Tadbir and Itq by Co-Owners
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tadbir and itq by co-owners

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions on tadbir divisibility and derive the compensation rules for co-owners in a shared slave scenario.

Core Idea
Tadbir's divisibility determines compensation rights among co-owners — Abu Hanifa allows it, Sahibayn do not.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute where three co-owners of a slave have differing actions: one makes the slave mudabbar, another frees him, and the third is silent. The key question is whether tadbir is divisible, affecting who owes what to whom. Abu Hanifa deems tadbir divisible, leading to reciprocal claims; the Sahibayn view it as indivisible, making the mudabbar owner of the whole slave and liable for two-thirds compensation.

Guided Path
1
Map the parties and their actions
Identify the three co-owners: the first declares tadbir (مدبر) while wealthy, the second then frees the slave (عتق) while also wealthy, the third is silent. The silent partner and the mudabbar seek compensation.
The order of actions is crucial: tadbir precedes itq.
2
Understand the disputed principle: divisibility of tadbir
The core legal question is whether tadbir (declaration of freedom upon death) can be applied to a partial share of a slave or must be applied to the whole slave indivisibly. This determines the status of each share after tadbir and the validity of subsequent manumission.
تجزى (divisible) vs. لا يتجزى (indivisible).
3
Apply Abu Hanifa's view
Under Abu Hanifa, tadbir is divisible. Each co-owner's share remains in his ownership. The mudabbar's act of making the whole slave mudabbar is an ifsad (corruption) of others' shares. The silent partner may claim one-third of the slave's qin value from the mudabbar. The mudabbar may claim one-third of the mudabbar's value from the manumitter.
Mudabbar value = 2/3 of qin value. Example: 27 dinars qin → 18 dinars mudabbar; claims: silent gets 9, mudabbar gets 6 from manumitter.
4
Apply the Sahibayn's view
The Sahibayn hold tadbir indivisible. The entire slave becomes mudabbar for the first to declare. The later manumission is void. The mudabbar must compensate both other partners with two-thirds of the slave's value (one-third each), regardless of his financial status.
No reciprocal claim; the mudabbar is the sole owner after tadbir.
5
Compare the practical outcome
Using the numerical example (27 dinars), compute net transfers under each view to see the difference in who bears the loss. Under Abu Hanifa, the mudabbar pays 9 to silent but receives 6 from manumitter, net loss 3. Under Sahibayn, mudabbar pays 18 to both partners (9 each), net loss 18. The silent partner gets 9 in both views, but the mudabbar's burden differs.
The thamarah al-khilaf is in the distribution of compensation.

ایک غلام تین آدمیوں میں مشترک تھا ایک نے مدبر بنایا اور وہ خوشحال تھا پھر دوسرے نے آزاد کیا وہ بھی خوشحال ہے پھر تاوان چاہا ساکت کیلئے اختیار ہے کہ مدبر کرنے والے کو رقیق کی تہائی قیمت کا ضامن ٹھہرائے اور آزاد کرنے والے کو ضامن نہ بنائے و اذا كان العبدبين ثلثة نفر فدبر احدهم وهو مو سرتم اعتقه الأخرو هو مو سر فارادوا الضمان فللساكت أن يضمن المدبر ثلث قيمته قناو لا يضمن المعتق وللمدبران يضمن المعتق ثلث قيمته مدبر اولا يضمنه الثلث الذى ضمن وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وقالا العبد كله للذي دبره اول مرة ويضمن ثلثي قيمته الشريكيه موسرا كان او معسرا ترجمہ و اگر ایک غلام تین آدمیوں کے درمیان (مشترک) ہو۔ پس ان میں سے ایک نے اسکومد بر کر دیا۔ حالانکہ یہ شخص خوشحال ہے۔ پھر دوسرے نے اس کو آزاد کر دیا اور یہ بھی خوشحال ہے۔ پھر انہوں نے تاوان چایا۔ تو خاموش رہنے والے کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ مدبر کرنے والے کو خالص رقیق کی تہائی قیمت کا ضامن بنائے اور آزاد کرنے والے کو ضامن نہ بنائے اور مدبر کرنے والے کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ آزاد کرنے والے سے اس غلام کی تہائی قیمت بحساب مدبر ہونے کے تاوان لے اور نہ ضامن بنائے اس کو اس تہائی کا جس کا وہ خود ضامن ہوا اور یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ پور اعلام اسی شخص کا ہے جس نے اس کو سب سے پہلے مدبر کر دیا تھا اور مدبر کرنے والا اس کی دو تہائی قیمت اپنے دونوں شریکوں کو تاوان دے گا خواہ وہ خوشحال ہو یا تنگدست ہو ۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ سے پہلے یہ ذہن نشین کر لیجئے کہ مدبر کی قیمت شریعت کی نظر میں رقیق ( غلام محض ) کی قیمت کا دو تہائی ہوتی ہے۔ مثلاً اگر غلام کی قیمت ۲۷ دینار ہوں تو مدبر کی قیمت ۱۸ دینار ہوں گے۔ اب صورت مسئلہ پر نظر ڈالئے صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک غلام تین شخصوں کے درمیان مشترک ہو ۔ پھر ان میں سے ایک نے اس کو مد بر کر دیا ۔ حالانکہ رقیق محض کی تہائی قیمت کا ضامن بنا دے اور آزاد کرنے والے کو ضامن نہیں بنائے گا اور مدبر کرنے والے کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ آزاد کرنے والے سے مدبر کی تنہائی قیمت تاوان لے لے اور جس تہائی قیمت کا وہ ساکت کے لئے ضامن ہوا تھا وہ آزاد کرنے والے سے نہیں لے سکتا ہے۔ مثلاً غلام خالص کی قیمت ۲۷ دینار ہیں تو مد بر کی قیمت اس کی دو تہائی یعنی ۱۸ دینار ہوں گے۔ پس مدبر کی قیمت کا ایک تہائی 4 دینار ہوئے اور غلام خالص کی قیمت کا ایک تہائی 9 دینار ہیں۔ پس حاصل یہ ہوا کہ مدبر کرنے والا شریک آزاد کرنے والے سے ۶ دینار تاوان لے سکتا ہے اور ۹ دینار بطور تاوان نہیں لے سکتا اور یہ قول حضرت امام اعظم رحمہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا ہے اور صاحبین نے کہا کہ پورا غلام اسی شخص کا ہے۔ جس نے اس کو سب سے پہلے مدبر کر دیا تھا اور بعد میں آزاد کرنا باطل ہے اور مدبر کرنے والا اس کی دو تہائی قیمت اپنے دو شریکوں کو تاوان دے گا۔ خواہ یہ مدبر کرنے والا خوشحال ہو یا مفلس ۔
A slave was shared among three persons. One made him mudabbar while he was wealthy. Then another freed him while he was also wealthy. Then they demanded compensation. The silent one has the option to hold the mudabbar liable for one-third of the value as a qin (pure slave) and not hold the manumitter liable. And the mudabbar has the option to hold the manumitter liable for one-third of his value as mudabbar and not hold him liable for the third for which he himself became liable. This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two companions said: The entire slave belongs to the one who first made him mudabbar, and he pays two-thirds of his value to his two partners, whether the mudabbar is wealthy or in straitened circumstances. Translation: And if a slave is shared among three persons, and one of them makes him mudabbar, and he is wealthy, then another frees him, and he is also wealthy, then they seek compensation. The silent one has the option to hold the mudabbar liable for one-third of the value as a pure slave and not hold the manumitter liable. And the mudabbar has the option to take from the manumitter one-third of the value as mudabbar as compensation, and he does not hold him liable for the third for which he himself became liable. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The two companions said: The entire slave belongs to the one who first made him mudabbar, and the mudabbar pays two-thirds of his value to his two partners, whether he is wealthy or in straitened circumstances. Explanation: Before the case, note that the value of a mudabbar in the eyes of the Shari'ah is two-thirds of the value of a qin (pure slave). For example, if the slave's value is 27 dinars, the mudabbar's value is 18 dinars. Now consider the case: A slave is shared among three persons. One of them makes him mudabbar, and he is wealthy. Then the second partner frees him, and he is also wealthy. Then the silent partner and the mudabbar partner seek compensation. The silent one has the option to hold the mudabbar partner liable for one-third of the value as a pure slave and not hold the manumitter liable. The mudabbar partner has the option to take from the manumitter the value of the mudabbar as compensation, but he cannot take from the manumitter the one-third value for which he became liable to the silent partner. For example, if the pure slave's value is 27 dinars, then the mudabbar's value is two-thirds, i.e., 18 dinars. One-third of the mudabbar's value is 6 dinars, and one-third of the pure slave's value is 9 dinars. So the mudabbar partner can take 6 dinars from the manumitter as compensation, but cannot take 9 dinars as compensation. This is the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa. The two companions said: The entire slave belongs to the one who first made him mudabbar, and the later manumission is void. The mudabbar pays two-thirds of his value to his two partners as compensation, whether he is wealthy or in straitened circumstances.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding three co-owners of a slave when one makes him mudabbar (declared free upon the master's death) and another later frees him outright. The silent third partner claims compensation. The passage first states the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa: the silent partner may claim from the mudabbar one-third of the slave's value as if he were a pure slave (qin), but cannot claim from the manumitter. The mudabbar may claim from the manumitter one-third of the mudabbar's value (which is two-thirds of the qin's value) as compensation. The reason is that tadbir (declaration of tadbir) is divisible in Abu Hanifa's view; each co-owner's share remains in his ownership, and the mudabbar's act of making the entire slave mudabbar is a malfeasance (ifsad) against the others' shares. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that tadbir is not divisible, so the entire slave becomes mudabbar for the first person who made him mudabbar, and the subsequent manumission is void. Therefore, the mudabbar must pay two-thirds of the slave's value to his two partners as compensation (since he now owns the whole slave, he compensates them for their shares), and this is regardless of whether he is wealthy or poor. The commentary then explains the valuation: the mudabbar's share is considered two-thirds of the qin's value. The numerical example with 27 dinars clarifies the compensation amounts: the mudabbar pays the silent partner 9 dinars (one-third of qin value) and receives 6 dinars from the manumitter (one-third of mudabbar value), netting 3 dinars loss. Both positions are clearly stated, but the passage does not explicitly indicate which is the mufta bihi; however, the context suggests Abu Hanifa's view is the basis for the detailed explanation.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been declared by his master to be free upon the master's death.
تجزى (tatajazza): Divisible; refers to the legal capacity of tadbir to be applied to a partial share of a slave.
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee to pay compensation; here it refers to the obligation to pay the value of the slave share that was acted upon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, from whom can the silent partner (sakit) claim compensation?
A) From the mudabbar only
B) From the manumitter only
C) From both the mudabbar and the manumitter
D) From neither

Key Takeaway
The divisibility of tadbir determines the flow of compensation among co-owners: Abu Hanifa's divisible view leads to reciprocal claims; Sahibayn's indivisible view centralizes liability on the mudabbar.
